Of which one is that you do three cauteries, or four, in the same manner as we have shown before, binding according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the cautery on the liver that we have said earlier; and do not press too hard with your hand at all the cautery, lest the patient suffers from its weight on his back; and another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery for two nails, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the wound which is located near the mouse, or when the cutaneous symptoms come to the left side, and lifting the swelling according to the swelling, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries are according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After the fire cautery, instruct the patient to put two needles in flames until they are perceived from the other side, and then hold hot the cautery, and so have four cuts, if you see, cut all the cautery with three needles.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when he has gotten infected for a long time, and this is true what the other cures have said.
de ydropisie	of dropsy (dropsie = swelling caused by fluid accumulation).
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Fire is not effective for dropsy, except when done in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four fire cauterizations inside the boil, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one near the intestine, and two behind, near the spine, and one towards the buttocks; and let the cauterizations be very close to the spot of the hurt.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After letting the cautery burn for a long time, and not stopping the healing of the patient after the cautery, and if the wound does not heal quickly, then both the pain and the inflammation will set in with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery on the belly is like a nail that we have shown before; and for the back it is olive oil, according to what was placed there before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet.
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical and filled with a purulent fluid, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot between the auricular and metatarsal bones; and lift your hand with the cautery so as not to turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply into it, as this would result in fires like the one that consumed a city, and so you must perform the cautery in this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, make the cut on both legs twice the size of the sword's tip; and so perform the cautery in each leg at the point of the cutlery, one on either side of the knee, towards the front and towards the back, in the same manner as we have said.
de la menoison	of the house
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When stomach problems come from cold and moisture, so that the retained virtues and digestion, which are in the stomach and intestines, become blocked and cannot be cured by any other treatments; and you see the patient suffering greatly, with great weakness, then do as we have said before about cutting on the stomach, or cutery of the abdomen, at the cutery circle; and four cauteries near the subtle bone, under all subtle cauteries, and two cauteries on the hams.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abounding and the patient suffering, make fire cautery on the nail, and fire cautery on each ulcer, and two make fire cautery on the stomach of the large one, because the cure is beneficial when it has good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure for hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are located at the fundament or one or more, and are old and are of large cold moist corrupt humors, and if they have been treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit, then make cauteries: III on the spine of the back, which is all behind the almcade point, and a little and a little in triangulation, and I cauterize under the buttocks II times; and if you think that his stomach is cold, and the flesh does not cook, and the face swells, then one grants cauterization on the stomach, as it was said before, and I another on the liver, and I another on the mouse bone all over with clavicle cauterization; and leave the cauterization for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After a cure let the limb heal.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "theul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the flesh, use a cautery that seems like a razor, and then put it completely on fire on the cut flesh, holding your hand back so that the cautery comes to life at the root of the vein, without cutting; do this once or twice, and if there is much flesh, cauterize each one as we have said; after, cure with ointments until they heal. And if you cauterize a great cautery on the thigh, it will bring more help.
de plaie mal curee	of badly healed wounds
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the sick person cannot bear excision or suturing, as we will tell in their own time, if it comes to such a malady that he cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When any of them come to fistulas, and they are inflamed and rotten with putrid moisture and corruption, if you prove them all with a subtle test, and keep in mind how much the test penetrates into their depth.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After having shaved the cautery as sharp as a razor, and pouring it into the fistula according to the quantity that it has entered, repeat the cautery until the corrupt flesh is burned once or twice, depending on the amount of putridity; and be careful not to touch the nerve that is inflamed, and also beware of great hemorrhages.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the flesh of the rectum and intestine, be careful with them, and do not make those fiery burns in their chariot, but rather think they are not people; after curing them as long as they are healthy, if the intestines are swollen, and the matter is hard for a long time, then know that the intestines are healed entirely; if the matter does not dry out, know that they are putrid, and the bones decay quickly; thus, as we will say in their place.
de la maladie des reins	About the sickness of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of fire comes to the kidneys, and great swelling, and does not ease with women, then it is fitting that you apply cautery on both kidneys from one side and from another at the cautery clavicle as we have previously said; and if we make a puncture in the middle, so will do three cauterizations in line, and they will provide greater relief.
de la vessie	About the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from fire and moisture, if the patient holds urine, then he applies cautery in the part behind the bladder, where the hairs are at the navel, on both right and left sides, each cauterized as long as the nail of one finger; and he cauterizes behind the back, where it is needed, or two times; and so the clavicle cauterizations according to what has been previously said.
de la marris	Let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrix is cold and moist, and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their terms delayed; and when they come, if it feels great pain: then it is fitting that you make 3 cauteries around the throat, as we have said about cutting for the bladder, and 2 cauteries behind the back; and if they are made with a nail, as we have said.
de la hainche	For the hainche (or shoulder).
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the moist viscous discharge comes to the shoulder joint, and because of this cause it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the hip is longer than the other when measured together; and if there are many swollen departements in the vicinity, then you must cauterize the patient on the shoulder joint with 1 cautery similar to a circle, and look straight ahead into the joint as it turns, so that the joint is within the circle; and do the cauteries similarly to those done for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the fire cautery does not take effect, then make three fire cauteries of olive oil, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the other wounds; and treat the patient until he is safe.
de la dolor de la hainche	of pain from the heel
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes from the heel, and it is of cold and moisture, and the patient is cured with what we said in the division, but the treatment does not work, and the disease is old: then it is necessary to purge the sick person of thick humors, fetid pills, or other hard-to-break pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After making the cautery, and the way of applying the cautery is according to two manners: namely, by assembling hot medicines, and cautery with fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is done in many ways, of which one is that you cauterize above the root of the hawthorn tree; three cauteries are made according to this form, and with each cauterization, make great depth and space, and let there be a space equal to the thickness of two fingers between each cauterization, and it is called olive oil cautery; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle above the head of the hawthorn tree, for this reason, because there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, if the cauterization at the cautery of the circle that we have before mentioned in the dislocation of the hawthorn; but make it in such a way that the circles contain the entire hawthorn, and all the thick skin around it be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way to do it in sciatique, when the pain lies in the hawthorn, and does not reach up to the thigh or up to the knee.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	If it comes just to the thigh and knee, he must let fire cautery on the outside of the knee four times, to the left side one little; and let it be a cutlery cautery or burn the thickened part of the wound; and if the patient feels that the pain extends up to two feet or close to an inch, cauterize at that place where he feels the pain three points or four on the cautery which is called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is the case, if he makes more; and if he knows that the pain is under the joint towards the thigh, let him cauterize with the cutlery cautery or circular cautery; and take good care in all your cauteries not to burn the nerves and great arteries, and do not make the patient any greater nuisance and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen others who made fire cautery on the ankle of the foot, and let them grow until the leg was entirely flaccid, and also the toes, and they were perceived and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a treatment for the belly that led to death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make fire cautery in one and in the other, according to this method.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the doctors said in the cautery of the hunchback, why this is the way, make such a tool and put it on the head as big as an oarsman's thumb, or a little less, and place them between each other at equal distance, just one over the other with the space of a hemp thread; and they should be in two parts, and also like hazelnuts, and have a iron pin well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to heat so that it is entirely red and covered in serents, and then place it on the back of the sick hunchback, and turn towards its healthy side; and once he has been cauterized once, let him remain for three days; and then apply ointment of butter, and leave the wound uncovered for a long time after the treatment with binding.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albuscin says that we should use little of this cautery because of its sharpness, and since few people use it; and therefore all see that these are the best cauteries, which can be borne by him.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of medicine burns if you make an instrument between crossed threads in the quality where it falls on the margin of the door, and is made of iron or rain at a long length, and has two nozzles, and one half inch between each one, and according to the size of a doe; and so that they are open towards and above, and joined together in this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After the patient lies on his stomach on a bed of hazelnuts, instruct him to put your hand very heavily on the bed of hazelnuts; after putting between the two hot circles of water that have been heated for one hour in the fire pot, let him rest there for an hour or so, and suffer the pain and the burning from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	But it will leave mordication, also as of fire; and when the mordications do not pass, take your hand away with the instrument and lift up the bed of hot water, and let him rest for three days, and put on butter so that what is black from the ashes is extracted; and let him remain for three more days until he is purged by this, and then that would be the second aid after the treatment of ointments, until he is cured.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended just to the thigh or just to the knee, then make an instrument that is fashioned according to what you have done in the groin more frequently; and this is the manner of the hot treatment, and I have written it down in the matter of treating medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take a mixture of calamine and live charcoal, an equal amount of each, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	If it has a small opening in front so that the point of an arrow can enter; and put that pot into another pot well filled with melted fat, and put upon it calamine and charcoal and hot water, until there are two pots above the powder like you have taken and pressed to your hand; and then leave it in this way till it comes out hot and sharp or melted fat, then take all that melted fat, and pour it on top of calamine and charcoal as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And so if it is very wet and is administered in the movement of various medical works and cauteries of other members because it does all the work like fire, and with other medicines not well done, such as cauterizing the hair like theseseeds, honey, anacardi and salt with soap, all these sweet things together assemble.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galiens tells us of a cure about one man who was cured of the pain in his groin and sciatic region, and great praise for it, and says that no other cure was needed, and he recovered once when this cure was performed, and he got baptized as he teaches here after.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And in this manner, take fresh and green lime juice and wet it down with a little fat, and crush it much with a spoonful of grease, and put it on the groin and on the thigh or where the pain lies, and bind it; and let him stay for three hours, by the quantity that the patient feels no more itching.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then put him into the bath until his body is somewhat softened, and put him into bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And so it is learned that no one should use cautery of these medicines unless after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when a varicose vein is cauterized with horse chestnut leaves, great pain will come on; and it must be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and anoint it with old oil, and put it on the crevice between the little toe and the great toe, which is called the fissure.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking dried horse chestnut, and anointing it with fire until it is charcoal, and put linen on it, and let it dry until it stains; and do this again, and do not stop doing so until you think by sense that it comes just to the hinch, and that the pain is ceased; for this manner of cauterizing is called "cautere of horse chestnut".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or by percussion or by great evacuation, or by appearance of matter spread out cold, none of these appearances is worth cauterizing, except for that which arises from an infusion of cold material.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is fitting after this that patients have a voiding of fetid pills or other appearances, and on them you make three lines above the back, where the pain lies, three lines in each according to virtue and quantity that the patient can bear; and it is done the cauterization in the form called "poins"; and if seen, do III cauterizations or IV at the clavicle middle according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This sickness comes to small children many times, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a straight line when they rise, and fear; and you will find in the lower spine on the back and in what appears on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and observe how it is cured, if the fire cautery is applied to the cautery of the cell according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the cautery stains each part of the spine in proportion.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that the fire is applied inside the spine to the cautery point, two lines or three, and the points are close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the treatment the limb should be kept until it is cured according to what we have said, and take care not to apply fire cautery in a gout or nerve pain.
de la dolor des jointes	of the joints' pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is caused by moisture that has expanded in each limb of the body, and when pain comes to the foot, they call it "podagre" precisely, and when it's due to cold cause and medicines can't cure it, then it's cured with cautery in this way: make a cauterization with cautery around the joint of the foot, and use olive oil according to that form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a wound that you prick on the face of the foot, make cauterization all over the cauterization which we claim "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the groin and in other joints, and this happens many times, then make cauterization on each groin III cauterizations or IV on each part, all the olive cauterization; and if you need more, then do more, but don't hold onto your hand burning until the swellings of the heat are dry.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the groin and back, the fire cautery that we mentioned in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make pains to press two fingers; and if there is no pain at all, make pains on each joint and on the skin of the hand; and if pains come to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and make good governance for the patient with various medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	But if you make good governance and purge the swelling, it will bring the patient to safety with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the wound of a stroke.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a wound comes in gangrene, and the bowels descend to the groin and it's new, then if you wish to cure his eyes, do not treat him on that day; and use things that clear his stomach, so the pus descends from its belly; after, make him sit on his back between your hands, and he commands you to tie his ankle so tight that his wound is healed, and take it to your feet, and sign with a mark that resembles half of a circle above the body; then take off the cautery in this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	Until he is white and feels pain.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then tighten the bowels to their place; and let the surgeon grasp his hand so that they do not return to their original position; and well treat the patient with ointments and attendants on his knees, and another on the lower part of the thigh which is pressing on his hands; then apply the cautery to the sign made on all fingers, and his right hand and his left hand until you pierce the bone, and if you do not pierce it the first time, so that it reoccurs again in another place until you reach the bone; and be careful not to let the bowels burst while you are doing the cautery; lest you burn them; and so that the patient does not die, or suffer from any other malady.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know this, when you do not come close to the bone with the fire cautery, your efforts are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is fitting that the cautery for children should be subtle according to their measure, and for great men also according to their size; after three days cure them with balm until the blister has fallen off; after treating other ointments until they are cured, and rest the patient forty days on his back so that the wound is well healed, and it is fitting that their nourishment be prolonged for a long time, so that the boils do not come up when they go out to chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, provide him with a well-made bandage and apply it for forty other days; and let him have good rest, so that he does little work and avoids excessive drinking and eating, and too much lifting of the head; and when he follows this teaching, he is entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say this after your treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the surgical incision on the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When such incisions occur in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not swell again, cut the incision according to its size, and remove one-third of the dead tissue; after the treatment as we have said; and none of the ancients said that it should be cauterized at the three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the level of the incision and draw a line for its width above the incision, and another below, and make the cauterization with your hands all around the knife.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and less painful.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of olden pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, whether by a fall or an injury, and this pain lasts for a long time, and the remedy of medicine is not helpful, then it is necessary to cauterize with the cautery which is called "poins", and perform the cauteries according to the length of the limb and its thinness and weakness and virtue and location of twists and of pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the pain is alleviated by the first cautery, it's good; but if that doesn't work, perform another cautery on the same spot, because in this fashion it must move to the limb that is nearest, so that you make the cauteries as long as the patient is sane.
de meselerie	Of surgery
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The trouble is not cured by cauterization with great help, and even the same illness that comes from the putrefaction of worms and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see the cauterizer, be careful if the illness is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not stop or stay there, and doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the whole patient, then apply cautery on the head: I cut off the top of the nose, and the other towards the front of the cheeks; two on each cheek, and one behind the ear; and leave your hand there until the cauterization comes to bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the great humors can escape; and cautery on the mouse according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the surgical instruments are everywhere scattered; and they manifestly belong to those cauterizations that we have said before the head, and one cautery in the flesh, and two on the spine of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one on the ribs and another on the loins, and two on the shoulders, and two on the groins, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the cavities of the hands; and beware of those that are on the inner edge of the derrière calcant, so that you do not burn them; and at no time perform a cautery on the bone of the finger, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that as long as you do more cauterization, the more good it does and profit is made; and know that patients do not feel pain from cauterization if they are already sick like the healthy person, because the body is entirely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the fire cautery be large and small according to the limbs and joints, as you will find in various types of metal tools.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the treatment let him eat the patient's porridge with honey and other remedies until he is sane.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling occurs in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it does not heal, then perform fire cauteries on the member according to its size and shape; and if the cautery goes into the flesh a little, in the swollen part, then treat him with bandages until he heals.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes it is done to cauterize with one hand and foot and back, after the outcome of the nerve that mutes the limb, and thus if there is swelling, it will come out; and no one should get in the way unless he knows about the limbs and the ways of moving the bones.
de albaras	Of the fire cautery
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called “albaras” is old and the art of medicine is worthless, then cut it with fire cautery a little at first, in proportion to the size of the boil, until the skin is fallen off, and its color changes; then give the cure of flour mixed with beans and lentils with olive oil and plantain leaves, and salt of coloquint and saltpeter, each one a part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and let him eat as long as he is healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure for the chancre by fire cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the chancre comes on, and you stop looking at it, if you cut it with fire cautery to fit around the circle of the chancre all the way to its edge.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all the wise men say that we should do cautery also in the middle of a chancre; and I don't think this is good, because I fear it will cause ulceration and corruption, and I have never wanted to try it before, and there is no more dire thing than being cauterized inside, like the "circle" cautery, as we said about many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of an edema that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some people have a disease called "adubelati", and it delays death because of its excessive flow or because the patient is very old (meaning they are very weak) with little blood, or because time passes slowly; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize inside using many small cauteries; after that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	She will hasten her death.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see her pierced with the fire cauterization, so that she is burned because of this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand at the middle of this sick disease called "adubelati" so that the fire cauterization pierces the liver, and let it be such that the patient feels pain in this manner so that the course of putrefaction is delayed.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until he becomes perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cauterization by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease that is called "corrodens", and it's nothing but an ulcer on a limb, because it eats the limbs just as the fire eats dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in someone who can suffer fire cautery, then inflate the cautery clamps very little and great, according to what is suitable for the patient or the disease; after cauterizing from all parts until you reach the whole corruption, and nothing remains, that which is corrupted should be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let him stay for three days, and put on the patient's cauterized wounds to suffer with fire-burning coal with oil until the burns from the heat are healed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of ointments produced charcoal.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that no healthy child is born, it's good; and if not, restart cauterizing on the one who remains corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this disease is sometimes cured by medicine in its place instead of fire cautery, but the fire cautery is of greater aid; and I have said before that the treatment for water-based medicine is done through division: take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of periwinkle flowers which come to the joints.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Very often the joints, by their own nature, develop a disease called "closure" according to our intention, and it is a great evil that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And there are two kinds of fire cautery for this disease.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you should heat the needle as if it were a hot iron, and let it be made of good steel to the size that can penetrate the nail in all parts, and have subtle margins; after that place it on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it becomes hot like the nail; then leave it for three days so that it starts to produce pus; afterwards make an ointment of fresh marjoram ground with vinegar, and let the ointment be on all the surface, and the nail will fall out and will be descaled from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to bind their limb with linen cloth until it is sound.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they have been burned by fire and suffer greatly in the body, and frequently happen to hands and feet, it is advisable to apply hot water cautery; and it is done in this manner: take a twig of tin or iron, or a quill of lead, and put on the clot and nail, as if to prick warts; and place the twig so that it comes into contact with everything around, then put some hot water on it, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand in turning so that the margin of the twig comes to touch the root of the nail, and can find its way through to the depth of the root; and suffer the patient for a little while under the cauterization of the hot water an hour; then leave it thus, and it will be drained of all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Instruct him after another, until you have looked at all those who are inside the body, then treat the limbs that obstruct the air.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people are shivering from cold or fever, or quartan fever, or any other, it is fitting that you make IV cauterizations on the spine of the back, I cauterization between each spine; and I cauterization on the neck, and I cauterization on the stomach to the olivary; leave them to shiver, and hasten their recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of festering ulcers
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No time ever does the body produce swellings or ulcers by chance, but rather they come from gross and corrupted materials.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it should be the first time when they appear that one makes cautery on each head of the pimple: a subtle cautery of fust wood, so that the point may be grasped by fire, or from the root of aristologe long, or with the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at no time do they cauterize while it appears, according to this method, and they cannot grow any new ones in front of them, but the superfluousness that comes from them is broken, and they are healed; but it should be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When an artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often great bleeding of the artery that is cut at the wound occurs, or from the incision of the abscess, or from the cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stink.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Instruct the patient to let whatever has happened at no one's fault be done quickly; if he hastens to put his two fingers on the wound of a vein, and strains himself much until it is appeased under his two fingers, and no more gout comes out; then put the cautery oilivaire in small and large quantities until they are all red; then take II or one or a little according to the size of the wound and how the arteries run, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your two fingers, and keep it there until it is not strained again.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	If he jumps over the fire when you lift your two fingers off the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then take hastily another from the cauterized ones that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after the other until he is strained no more; and beware that you do not burn the nerve which is near, and that no other harm befall the patient; and know that when there is no bleeding from an artery, it cannot be well closed itself when the arteries are large, unless by one of the four ways we have mentioned: either by cautery, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by very tightly tying with thread, or by medicines placed on them which have power to close wounds; and so he is bound and strained inevitably.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will restore a swelling of a tightly wrapped limb or put hot things on it, or other similar things, if they do not profit from it.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone, and they do not have any remedy or medicine present, he must put his two fingers on the wound of the vein, just as we said, and tighten it so that the swelling remains above the wound and above the vein; and let him not move at all, but let him apply cold water frequently until he is frozen stiff and swollen, and solidified; and do the necessary cuts in front of what he needs for cautery and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Now begins the second book on the treatment of tumors.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	As we said in the first chapter about all diseases because of which it is necessary to apply fire or hot medicine, cauterizations, ointments, and the causes and strumous matter and forms of cautery; and as I mentioned earlier in this very book, I will now go through this same way for those things that are often treated more easily by what we have written.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than with the first cautery, and therefore you must take greater care.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you, do not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come in for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	But those who come from those who have suffered greatly because of their illness die quickly due to the harshness of their illness, and the severity of its evil; and from this one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And from these ones who are doing their own thing, and saying "wait, I am cured"; and the sick person is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you should consent only to those who come to you and have this manner, but put more emphasis on your honor than your greed, and be neither too weak nor too foolish, but wise of what you are certain of, and of what you can gain from it; and use prophecy and indication in the treatment of your sick patients to see if health will be restored; for that will help you to achieve good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three dear children, Our Lord gives you good understanding and straightness of mind, and if it is your will to aspire to the holy inspiration from his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I instruct you to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Until it is filled with water.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Recognize that this illness often comes from children to infants, and when the child is restrained too tightly around the head; and there is no known reason for it.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness occur except in children, and all those that I have seen it has shortened their life; and therefore it seems to me that it would be worth spending a great deal of time on treating it.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw an infant of that sort, whose joints were swollen with water, and the head would become engorged every day so much that he could no longer support it; and I believed so strongly that he was dead, for this swelling was assembled beneath his bone, between his skin and the bone; and the abscesses are small, that you must cut into the bone with a large incision; and so long as the swelling runs, make it just as long as II we have measured.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more deep, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the manner of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the commissures of the jaw on each side, and blood spurts when you press your hand into it, and that does not stop: then it is fitting to make three incisions in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, take out all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After binding the incisions with cloth and powder, and putting vinegar and oil in, and letting it that way for five days; then take out, treat the wound by poultices and bandages, and let the head drain more, and afterwards give to the patient dried meat of half an inch of moisture so that the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	In another way of incision, you look at or open the size of the abscess and its assembly, because it is sometimes in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right side, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So then when you cut in or open the abscess, and fill it with water, and do it according to what you have the power; and be sure not to cover the artery; and watch for blood flow, so that the patient may die from the bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of the shoulder.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens that there is no disease called "caterre" in the eyes or at the nose, and the illness is old and medicines do not help, then a late cure is applied, which is to cauterize with what is like cutting both arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Instruct the patient to cover his eyes before doing so; after he has rubbed his head with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then extract the patient's neck with two cloths; then look out where the vein is located, and the necks of one and the other are behind the ears, and they are not returned; then sign the necks of the ligature, then cut one and the other with a good spoonful of II parts, until the vein reaches just to the bone, and so be done by rubbing it large on the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, pour out the spoonful below the artery and cut it above, in the same way as it should be traversed.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut open, if you let him jump without any head continuous movement.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
de emigrainne	Leaving behind
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient inflammation comes in, and catarrh is gone, because of moisture from tears and heat in the temple and old sores similar to these, and it is treated with various medicinal remedies and none of them help, if we cut out the arteries of the temples and cauterize the joints, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is such that the patient will make bald spots on his temples, and listen to the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well with its beating, and is not easily closed as in many men who are very cold; if it is closed, then strangle the neck of the patient with some cloth, then rub the skin with any harsh cloth, and apply hot water until the artery becomes manifest.
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Instruct the patient to burn the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then take it up towards the top with pincers, and depart from each part well because they are stuck to that side; and if the artery is subtle, twist it at the point of the needle, then cut from that side according to the quantity of two thumbs.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	But if it is not cut, let it go without any pain whatsoever throughout.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And bring the blood out from six fingers, just with three; and if the artery is large, it is best that you tie it in two fingers of a strong double thread of silk, so there will be no purulence in front of the wound at the time of the healing, and the bleeding will cease; then cut the surplus between the two ligatures in the same hour, and if you see, since this is the cauterization with the surgical knife up to the bone until the fingers are cut, it is the gentle work, if the patient does not have fever and it has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is aid to finish off moisture: for this it has more aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary to extract the arteries, you fill him with a vein of old cotton and put on well-made tourniquets; and when you loosen them, if they are treated with dry medicines that produce charcoal, and with tourniquets, until he is healed; and if without cutting the artery, as you work, you hasten to cover with fire cautery, or you apply a vein of vitriol and strain it on your hand until the blood stops; and if you do not have this present, you put on the vein your must to him, until he is frozen stiff, and then raise him in cold water until it ceases, and tie him as necessary; for what is more tender and easier to extract the artery than cauterizing the vein with a cautery of two parts, but the tourniquets are well spaced to last longer their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the urine is too cloudy, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have two large pins, then when you press the bandages against both sides, and you heat the iron so that it comes into contact with the bone, cut the vein in two; and let the distance between the two incisions be since there is no cauterization to be done on this entire procedure; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are falling into the veins that are on the forehead and crown of the head, and he does not benefit from any medicine we make, and you see the face of the sick person become red, and feel as if his front leg has been struck; and when the skin is wet and moist so much that the hairs are falling out, and are burned by the heat of the tears, it may be necessary for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	Instruct the patient to call them "cure contused", and you should make him re the hairs on his head that he has or in front, then make three incisions on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as two fingers together above the nose, and the other two with two fingers apart over the papers, and avoid the incision of the arteries that are at those two places over the papers; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and let each wound be three times through a joint; and have prepared an amount of sponge and cloth to absorb the blood, then pour the good spatula into two parts as is the form.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.
