From the incision on the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the wound that is between the two incisions until the full thickness of the flesh above the bone, then take another part from the middle incision up to the other second, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If it is boiled in the first cut with the instrument called "culterial", and is well cut from one side and the other, soft but not cutting, that's its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And cuts the skin with the knife towards the raw flesh at the point, and the skin is soft towards the bone, and boils until it comes to the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And chops all the vessels that flow from the head through the eyes until the incision is continuous just as close to the wound, and then another cut in the middle cut just up to the other edge; and then draws out the blood equally, presses the cloth on the blood taken; and puts a square piece of cotton wool on each cut, and lays a wet cloth on top in wine and oil and ash, and keeps away the pus from coming back; and on the third day unties the bandage, and gives it a great dose of aqua tedia, then the cure with oignement basilicon with olive oil, and other cures for wounds, until he is sane.
dou reume des eulz	Do something to the eyes.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any vein is infected, and you see the eyes cloudy and red, and weaken the sight, and the paper burns; and the hair falls out, and pain sets in on the forehead, and the patient coughs; then from these accidents you can see that those matters and this catarrh do not come but from many veins, and the female cure if it is, so let us know this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to tie their forehead, then make a great cut in the middle of the forehead, and another small one near.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And commence from the incision of the left temple to the right temple; so that the cutting is just until the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move to the lower part; and when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with an sponge, then sew between the two lips of the incision with a clean cloth made of linen; then tie the above moist cloths in wine and oil, and be careful not to let pus form; when it has healed, you should rub the bone so that the discharge begins to come, then treat with purgatives which make the bowels move.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	Take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of powdered cinnabar, and make them paste; and administer this in the wounds to stop pain throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the evacuation of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grain, or hair, or stone from the mine, or similar thing like metal; or seed, such as jisses, fevers, peas; or fluid-like substance such as water and pus, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	If he falls into the ear stone or another kind of thing that does not adhere to the ear and will not grow in the ear, put his ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill a small amount of violet oil or sesame oil, and administer extraction; and then make him vomit with conditons, and put the nose closed when vomiting comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool into the ear, and make the ear towards above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often comes a disease by this treatment; and if it does not come, take out the extractions with subtle pinches, for thus is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps off with the pinches, that's good; if not, take out an excision at the lump with a small double fold; and if it doesn't jump by this, make a cauldron of resin and pour hot water into the head through the ear hole or opening very hard, and soothe what is within the cauldron made of molten wax so that the venom cannot enter through the cauldron; then pull out the form, for often it comes off as we have said; and if it doesn't come off in this manner, take a glue to catch it and before catching them, put something on which is sharp enough to pick up the ointments, and put some cloth around; then press the glue onto the bone or whatever thing is there, and pull out the form.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot be cured of all these things that we have said, then hasten to pierce the ear sooner than an abscess on the cheek vein, and spasms; and the manner of the piercing is that you first make the patient healthy from the cephalic, and extract the blood according to its virtue, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat where it depends; and the cut shall be as a crescent moon, until you arrive at the bone, then pierce according to your power, and suck out hastily into your mouth; and the cure shall continue until he is cured.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is pus that has formed and it inflames, then extract the pus; and if it cannot come out, then administer a subtle instrument in the shape of this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And instruct to make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make this cut when you think the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, as many times as you have done so; then take out the small pieces with fine forceps and vinegar, just as we have said, in such a way that the extraction will be light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In water then whatever is put into the ear should be used for ear drops of conditios first, and fill the ear with wool.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And if it becomes infected on that same ear or in the water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she falls for that, then it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If this does not work, if she pricks many pieces according to the length of your head should be tender and light, and let it burn slightly for a while; and put the patient an earplug or a plug in her ear, and walk on both its sides, and take fear from one side, and hit a stone from the other side, onto the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease doing this of piece to piece until the water is completely gone, and so she falls completely; and if you see, prick it with an arrow, and inject one of the needles into the ear, and the other on the head by fire, until the most tender point is burned; then make another part of other joints as long as the water has completely passed, just as we have said in the piece.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of meat, if it is of small body, like pus and similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body and can be felt, take out the excrescence with pincers; and this is the lighter thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ear, mark the ear while you cure it as we have said in the division and when treating distillations; for if the cure does not work, so that you should look at the ear towards the sun: if there are no worms, take out the canal with subtle pincers; and if there are none, pierce the eardrum because this is the form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it may be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And pour the most subtle head into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then suck form after form until they all come out; do this often enough that all will exit.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, as I have said in the stone; and if they still block like we have said, administer dilutions just as the old ones have used in the removal of worms, and you will find or use dilutions; and pour your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, because this is the form which you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And if it is silver or lead, pour them down into the small openings, and then over the surface to dilute; and in order to press the mixture within the instrument well-made for this purpose, and if you see the razor and a piece of cloth on the point, then pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the tube, into the ear; then pour the contents of the razor into all the cloth, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or almost come out of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and so the distillations be heated over the fire as well as when they are poured into the ear; and keep them not too cold, for the medicine would not be very good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the bursting of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any holes in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults as a result of bursting of an ear due to a wound or because something got stuck inside the ear, and sometimes there comes a complete rupture into the ear if one cannot see it, while at other times the hole remains small and does not hurt much.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	So when there is a complete rupture if one cannot see it, it is due to a disturbance of the health in many ways, and in this case you should put the ear of the sick person in the sun; and look inside: if you see any bloody discharge or inflammation apparent, then the eye tells you that this has been going on for so long that its shape is like this:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And so are the stitches and threads before and behind every part, if not to cut the ear; if the operation is of charnel or flesh of the ear, if you have fine needles and carefully prick, and lightly cut until that flesh is all bone.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is in deep in the ear, then take a fine razor and lightly shave it, then put on flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the operation that the patients feel great pain in the ear, prick lightly, and guard that you do not grease the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to its large size and the hole, and cover with Egyptian gauze.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this on no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and gauze in rosewater, and powder on vitriol broken; and if you see that ear is swollen, cover it so that you treat the tent and move another tent moistened with rosin oil and wax, until the swelling is bone; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If blood comes out when they are being pricked, plunge an sponge into cold water and drap it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove swelling from bleeding which is in treating drainage.
de la char des papieres	Out of the ashes of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Clean the ulcer that comes from paper around the eyes when they are moist and dry, if it is necessary, stretch them with pliers and tweezers, and cut off its roots with a spatula, then apply vitriol to it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it does not heal without treatment, when you cauterize the lenticular part with a subtle cautery, and then cauterize after the incision is made; and they are repeatedly treated, so that nothing remains of their roots; and when those roots are cauterized by fire, they do not return again.
de la gresle	From the horse
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often come to paper from the eyes things that seem like warts in form and hardness, and because of this is called "grandine" disease, and it's an assembly of moisture thick on both sides; there are such signs: take care if the grandine moves from one side and the other, and it's a light thing to know; do it then by cutting large, then scorch each part lightly, then take with pins, and then hit.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	But if you cannot cover it by piercing into the paper, and do not grieve the patient; and if there is a big tear, then there is an edge to sew, and the treatment so long as it is cured; but if it's small, then don't make any force, because the treatments bring back pain soon and hurt the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	Et se li grandine is falling down inside of the ear towards the upper part, so turn the paper and feel the granules, and press them with pincers, and chop and press from one side and the other; and if the paper is separated by incision, nothing hurts; and when the granules are chopped, wash off the oil of salt water, and cure the ear of that which causes him to have a great stinging, until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fatty eyelids
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	There is a grease that is stuck in the webs of the eyelids above, and this often happens to children, with no one being able to see them, and it causes great pain to their eyes, and they come with catarrh in the mornings, and can't look at the light of the sun because the tears overflow onto their eyes; therefore, they lie on their faces, and sleep there, and have moist eyelids beneath their eyebrows that cause inflammation and appearance changes due to the exinach grease that opens up in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the elbow with your two hands and feel the swelling between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of applying this is that the patient places his head on your healthy one; and then take a linen cloth, and tie a tent around it in the shape of a circle according to the quantity contained between each part, then put it on; press with your two hands from one side and the other, so that the swelling is assembled inside the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the swelling at the junction of the skin, not making it larger than the wound you make on a vein; and sew around the flesh until you see the swelling; for more frequent instances, the swelling comes from the incision, in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take out then from the place entirely of this charpet cloth between your two hands at once; and turn your hand to the right and left so that it be spread; and guard that you do not add in the cut, lest you come near all the spectrum until the oil, lest you burn.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the vein does not open in the beginning of the cut, then make it slightly tight in the opening so that it appears; then cut as we have said, then bandage with cloth easily and wet, and apply to the limb, and strap around the waist.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who cut the rope and set it up to corrupt that remaining moisture.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer will make him sane.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to a swollen joint, then the doctor will apply plaster so that it heals.
des poilz des papieres	from paper hairs
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper hairs grow together in an unnatural way and become inflamed, they cause the eyes to be affected, and lead to various types of diseases such as tearing and swelling of the paper, and albugen (a yellowish discharge), so that it is a cause of destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways for treatment: either by heat cautery together with fire, or by astringent medicine according to what it is before the chapter of cautery, and done either by incision and suture or by cauterization, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the patient's head on a healthy one, then turn the paper of oil at your left hand; if it turns over, it is good; if not, if there is an arrow in the upper part, then cut off from above all the paper, and take the arrow out; then place under the paper a small linen cloth and drapery, then sew underneath the paper around the entire area, from the large lance to the small one; then pull out the arrow, and put under the paper a figure of encaustic, as with myrrh oil, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you see lifting the paper which is drawn on all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Instruct the patient to put on paper of great quantity according to how the paper is softened; then do all the procedures up to two lines that you have signed off, and begin from great care just as small; and let one of the incisions close near the natural hair in the growth of a root, then pour it into one of the two angles of ease, then scorch it whole; then assemble the two lips with a stitch of an awl to all thread of fine linen, and wipe off the blood, and do to dry the superficiality of the threads on both eyes at any sticky thing, if you have seen this done; and if not, since you do not care, then leave the stitching and the threads just three days or four; then cure the wound with stitching and constraining, for the paper relives at the moment of the wound and the assembly of it, but the stitching is weak (as they say the ancients), and this is work with fear; and if there is another manner: and it is that you know the paper of a figure which is like the navel of myrtle, as we have told, at three points according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off what overhangs with equal cuts according to the form that is there:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps firmly, and they are not even, then take an awl or have a thread of some sort, and tie it around the figure; and take another thread from the larger limb, and another from the smaller, and assemble them evenly between your two fingers; then fix your hand evenly, and fix all the skin where you have stitched, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suturing, and treat until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar ointment; and sometimes happens that the hair of the scalp are converted: so it should be noted that you use what we have said about incising; but the suture in one and both is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the cains is according to this form: and it is that you will convert the paper and the skin inside as I have said, and then do II caines by art, and II subtle ligatures as long as the paper and the skin are; and cut as II joints of II parts wherever you hold the fillets; then assemble one and the other subtlety on what overcomes from the oil-paper, and strain the two cains from the two parts in form; and leave it so for some days, and the cure which is strained will mortify and necrotize and bring forth, whatever it cherishes by it.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if you cut with force, then the cure will continue until he is healed; and when the wound is sewn, and the skin is raised, and the hairs no longer cling, that is the form of the II caines that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Instruct the patient to prick at their hair with a fine needle and put a thread of soft silk into it, then tie the hairs together one by one softly, so that the long ones are about a palm's length; then insert another fine thread of silk quickly into the chase, not over the chief; then have the patient's chief in your safe hand; so that they may see the opening if they wish, for this is a subtle and small operation, then prick the needle into the whole chase at the root of the hair added together, and make it pierce into the paper quickly until you draw it out above the natural hair; then pull out the hair until the roots come to the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	Instruct the patient to treat and let go of the chase if the hairs do not come forth with it, so you will treat the chase below all the thread that you have ordered, until the chase is worn out of its place and you see it through the vision of oil; then you will treat the chase and the thread, and crush the oil and let go II days or III, until the hairs grow in their place and are born with the hair on top; and if the hairs are small, accompany I long hair from the chest, nature-wise, and raise it with that one which you leave, until it is stretched out and then lift.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil's rot
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease that is called "aleacrati" or the rot comes into the oil, there are two kinds of it: one natural and one unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And happens by sudden blow, or cut, or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way of the work in it is that you cut through the scar, and tend to the lips, and put in linen tents, and bind them until they are healthy; and it is not advisable to use in the treatment of wounds things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	But if you do this, the sickness will return worse than it was before; however, works of softening things are done, like fenugreek; and an arse is moistened with water or oil and a seed of flax is cooked; and ointments made from melted diyaquilon in any of the oils, are applied to this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you guard yourself from it so that it does not harden again according to its original form; and this work that we have said is not one than can be done in advance of this sickness, which will return according to its original form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh which comes into oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is found under the skin and truly is called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from cuts and wounds, cauterization, and similar things; and the vein of the flesh is such that if you prick an arrow with it, where the thread has one double end, and pierce into the skin, starting from the left side to the right, until the thread reaches two fingers of the flesh; then stretch the skin above all the way up to the tip of the needle, and cut off at one span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the skin of the paper returns according to what is needed, it's good; but if not, take a razor and put it in the cut, turn the skin, and make two cuts on either side within the skin; and let the joints of the two cuts meet at the two angles of the incision you have made; and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter which has no «I griesche»; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity of its parts below, of what is outside the skin, then sew together the two parts cut, with the price of one thread of linen; then give the cure of those things we have said about mild medicines and poultices, until he is cured.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	In case of the illness coming from cutting or stitching or cautery, it is fitting that you cut an open wound under the hairs of the affected skin, and according to what was said before; then sew between the two fingers of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, because it is very diverse in shape, and the wise masters make use of every possible method so that it may return to its natural figure; and the patient themselves, according to what they need of treatment and instruments in more severe dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Suddenly from the paper.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	So that this stitch has come to the hands with a certain manner, where the paper above is stuck with white of oil, and cannot move or do its natural things, if it so happens that you put the point of a file on the paper, and lift it up; and let it be sewn, with pinches, as long as you copy what is correct to the stylus fine, which should not be too rough nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot suffer from the stylus being too rough or stinging the oil; and so your incision, where you scrape off this assembled thing, gently, so that the paper returns according to its natural shape; and it is healed all that assembly, and there are no more times with oil hot water, and salted warm water, and cologne; then put between the paper and the oil a linen tent, and place above the oil linden oil wet in abundance of beeswax; and after three days use the cologne and such swift things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the blood of oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two kinds of joints: one is like a swollen nerve and similar to fat frozen solid, and another that is not swelled but similar to a cold, moist spot when touched with iron, and handled in the pan; it cannot be felt; and both seem to approach the large artery, and grow little by little until they cover all of the vein and all of the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of cutting is that the sick person puts his head on your healthy one, then he opens his eyes; and he lifts the paper to his hand, then cuts the vein as stitches with a little double suture, and exposes it above; then take an needle, and put in a horse's hair, or a veal's, or a cow's, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and push into the vein, and pierce all through the needle, and tie the vein with a thread and expose it above, and scorch all along the length of the vein until the purple and silk-colored part reaches his head, then cut off the remaining part at the root of the artery to all its subtle fibers and little forces, and leave nature's form or the artery, so that by cutting there will not come the blood of tears accustomed; and sometimes only the vein is tied up with a thread, as we said; and then scorch it so that this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	If the nerve is not numbed, and you cannot push the needle in, and the sinew will not enter, this condition often requires treatment with medicine; and just as I have told it in the division, if you see it covered, apply oil to the patient, and take the saffron lightly and sweet according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And then carefully extract the nerve under the surface; and if you see that it has not diminished at all, and the reason is pressing inside, mix oil from your mouth with a collier of litargire and red wine vinegar, and let it cool just as it was before; then resume the other work according to this same operation, until it is completely uncovered.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing troubles you with the oil, like a swollen joint, then take the milk and first cure the inflamed joint until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is also healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh on the arm is marked at night in the oil by great harm, then suspend it at once, and strike a part off not entirely, lest blood come from the eye; then distill oil with red wine that is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of flesh which is born on the nose
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	So that if the flesh of some men does not turn red at all, and covers the nose and restrains it on the paper and the thread without looking, and seems like a rosebud; and the wounds are such that the patient lays his head in your sound [i.e. healthy] shoulder, then open the eyes, and apply all that flesh to the nails, and hold them by force; then strike the first flesh, and go repeating at the razor until it is finished, and be careful not to bleed the oil on the wound; and do as we have said in the incision of the ulcer with spatumile, when you take out little pieces so that the form afterwards shows [i.e. heals]; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been removed, apply silk oil or distill wine of vinegar and seeming corrosive medicines, and put on the sound cotton with wool dye, if it be secure of the abscess; and if it remains nothing, and the pain will not subside, then leave the oil and cure the abscess with soothing medicines for the abscess; and so return to your wound till it is healed, and do thus treat the flesh bound in the oil by this semblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But in all cases it is necessary to take away the cure of each weak man from his natural road and accident road, in the presence of iron; and do not put your hand into any of these operations until you see that this limb suffers more from the operation.
des voines des eulz	of the eyelids
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	But these are veins of the eyes that are red and hidden beneath the skin, and they take away their vigor and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore to be done first that you look at the eye, in which vein it is, whether it is large or not, and if there is no other disease of fire than the eye; then do it thus: instruct the patient to put his head on a pure cloth, then suspend those veins all day according to your wisdom, and let them be subtle double according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two on one side by degrees in three parts according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil as forces those veins subtly, and suck the blood hour after another, until you see remove the veins' forces from the oil; and guard that you do not strike the oil with the points of the scalpels, and perform this operation at noon in front of the sun, and be very hot in your operation so that you only take out those veins; and when you have done this, then distill in the oil camphor green and red to corrupt what remains in the wound.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have power to coil all that in one hour, then do a plaster on the oil of soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and let it sit for some days until the pains are soothed, and ensure that there is an abscess hot, then continue according to this manner as long as he is healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	About the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The arrowed fistula: when you cure it by cautery and medicine, burning water according to what I said before, and it is not healed, there must be an infection in the one that you cut open, where it must die, and remove all the moisture that is in it until the bones are exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bones are exposed and you see the corruption and blackening, if the form is all the instruments of which this is made; and it is called "aspergh chief", and let it be fashioned in iron according to its head shape; and point it as sharp as a lime, as it is now in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put on the sharp iron over the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you know that this corruption has passed; and do this not again, then restore the bone with the medicinal extract.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	In case the sleeve is swollen and inflamed, and it is pressed tightly, and the body of the bow is swollen and remains so for 40 days, and it does not heal and does not break open, and accidents do not come from it, then you know that he is cured; if this is not the case, there is only one other option to return the fistula to the puncture in the nose according to this form: and therefore, you will uncover the bone for the second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, when you uncover him, so that you make an incision according to this form, and let the nails of iron be at three angles, and the fistula should be narrowed just as you see it.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then you put him on the bone of the scapula, and move your hand away from the wound for a little while, then turn to make a total incision through the wood until he feels the bone and perceives that it is coming in when he holds his hand over his nose; and therefore, restore the new of dry medicines as I have taught you, if they come to life and swell again, then pour the material into the nose; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the issue of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open all the time, and they do not come to relieve the pain of the head, or ease it, if you wish to treat the patient; then apply some oil, made of ice and aloe and frankincense and gum arabic, and then strain the oil, and apply the poultice on bandages and cloth; and the way of applying the cloths is that you take soft cloths, double each one in four, and then put one over another according to the amount they have need; then strain it above a hard strip, and renew the poultices to relieve pain; then remove the poultices and let the oil restrain for day and night, and if they apply ointment, so that you tie it tightly, if it is needed, tie it more; then remove the ointment after the day and night, and if you see the oil repaired, it is good; but if not, renew the poultice and cloths and the ointment and poultices until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The fall of the woolly hair
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes to the woolly hair, then it opens up and comes out like grains of resin, and it is amazing to see; therefore, if you cover the eye with gauze, the operations are such that you insert an needle in the root of the skin on top of those areas above, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the ear; and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its disposition; then cut out the leaden thread and tie one part of the wool tightly, and press well, then extract the needle and apply olive oil mixed with beeswax; and let it be so long as the threads stick to the wool, then treat the oil on soothing things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is tied by the wool around each quarter of a circular cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes do great appearance, so cut at the spot just behind where the oil flows from, and run to the moist area, and descend the eyes, and enter soon thereafter; then pull out as soon as they are clean.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil bowl
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness called "alcunnati" is not found in fires but in the oil bowl that is assembled there, resembling cold water flowing down, and it's not actually cold water; and the way of its appearance is such that you should sit the patient on a prepared seat straight up, then take hold of his head with two parts of your hands, and pull him so much as you see the oil coming to the top of your eyes; then place it in, do not let go and be crushed by the light, and see how the patient looks like they usually do; and if it doesn't come out downwards, know that it's cold water, and when the oil bowl is not assembled so as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you sit the patient between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and make above the corneal conjunctiva with the spatula in continuation of the conjunctiva and the crown, until the bow is straight; and when it is drawn out, if it has been put on a hot water or honey melted and butter, or fenugreek boiled and honey, then cure him with another cure until he is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen similar signs of water in the division, and what it is necessary to pierce; if according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your hands crossed, with fire from the light towards the sun, and tie the healthy oil very tight; then put paper of oil to one's left hand if his eyes are to the left, or to one's right hand if they are to the right; then take in one's right hand if his eyes are to the left, the instrument called "almagda", or with one's left hand if they are to the right; then put the tip of the instrument at the crown by the thickness of a thread in that paper of oil towards the lesser part of the minor margin, then pour the "almagda" instrument virtuously, and turn your hand until it pierces into the paper of oil, and feel that the "almagda" comes to the void; and it is necessary that the measurement of the path of "almagda" be at the full length of the measurement of the space from the plum's pit to the end of the nail; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the corneal tissue, then put the instrument just above it or where the auge is, then press with one direction after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the sickness descends now, so will he see the patient in front of him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After the patient has rested for a while, if the sickness returns on its second course, place the forceps with the instrument, and when it is fixed and does not rise, take it out gently in twisting motion with your hand little by little; then put back in its oil a little of the silver thread, and clean within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put in place the oil-soaked cloth or a moist linen in olive oil and plenty of wine, and bind with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Let us also, and those of our age, put on some common salt with plenty of wine.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the joint cannot enter into its place due to hardness because there are two types of people who have very hard joints, so it is advisable that you take up the instrument which is called "alberit", for this reason:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce the conjunctive alone, and do not go too deeply into it, but make the patient subtle, then pour in blood, as we have said; and when you complete the work, the surgeon attending will be present, because he sleeps on his back in a dark room; and you should restrain all movements, and give light food, and do not move his head or hand or foot, and it is advisable to bind him according to his disposition from now until three days; then release him into the same dark house, and test his vision, and make him see some things, and then set him free after seven days; and it is not advisable to do this in the patient's own room or after the incision now, but it is advisable to lighten him, because the water mounts quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	In case of an abscessed tooth, instruct the patient to remove the oil on the seventh day, and seek the advice of one who has knowledge of abscesses; and when it is appeased, lift the eye and put a poultice on its face to cover for each day, so that it may be dried in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then the pus comes out little by little, and converts into its cases; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Island of Ireland, who said that in some far-off lands, they do perform a certain operation involving amputation, because of the water, but I never saw it or knew of it in any books of the ancients; and by chance, it might be a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of maggots, because those who do not know them recognize them by sight; and they are from pure straw:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the head of this same subtlety, and the lower ones are three times in a row.
de la char sor le neis	of charcoal on the nose.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	They never grow or appear as different types of charcoal, because there are some that resemble scorpions almost to the point of being, and if they have charcoal encrusted with a red hue, and soft charcoal of a bone-colored tone.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	So when you find one of those soft (charcoal) ones that is not encrusted, it is necessary to sit the patient between your hands facing the sun; and work on his nose, and put the charcoal on those marks, and rub them with fire; for as long as you can sustain that subtle pressure from one side until you see that the charcoal is completely exposed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	In case there is no remaining part that can be covered, if you have all the minor strumens (smaller wounds) lightly treated, so that nothing stays; and without putting more pressure on it, or incising the flesh, cut as it seems to require; and if these are malignant ulcers, hasten and cauterize them until they are stopped bleeding and are no longer open, then throw out or remove them with vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose is closed and moisture comes just to the palace (the eye), check if it is sound; and if moisture does not come like it should, check if there is a bone underneath, because the wounds do not come from cutting: then it is necessary to put a thread of linen a little thick, and sewed by hands, with no space in between; and apply ointment on the child's wounds until it comes out through the nose into the mouth; and many times they do this to children at school, and it is a light thing for the one who does it; then hold the head that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other head which comes from the mouth with the other hand, and check each one after the other by feeling as if you are in the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make it as long as you know that the noose has not corrupted this hair, then take the child, clean the wound, and anoint the head in Egyptian ointment, and place it directly over the nose so as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments have corroded everything that is remaining of flesh; and then put on a bandage after some days, until he is cured, and if he needs dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, because one distills oils and medicines over the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And if it is made of silver or iron, resembling a lantern lid, like a bandage, and the conduit is done similarly; and if you see, do a bandage closed, and with instruments so that they can purify the head; and hold one hand over the head to keep it while you heat the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the head on the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	For the head on the neck there is often a sickness called "telul", and it grows and becomes large boils, until it is visible to look at; and for this reason you must copy the treatment from the beginning, and apply the cautery or hot medicine to it; and if one waits too long to treat it so that it becomes very large, if it is hard, it will turn red with pus: do not touch it with iron because that's an enchanted wound, because when you cut into it once, it brings great evil to the patient; and if the wound is soft in touch, not red with pus, and you see what can be covered, then make the patient empty his bowels and apply the treatment with fear, and treat the boils of dry things and straining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the neck is struck and crushed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	He knows that when a solution of continuity comes from one of these old cartilages, little is gained, however, for in few men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, if this happens to anyone, consider carefully whether the wound is fresh and full of blood; and then add two stitches on a suture, and treat him until he is cured. If the lips are swollen on one side and the other, it is advisable to scorch all the parts that are inflamed until they heal, then reassemble the two lips with a suture, tie them up, and sprinkle with powder of dragon's blood and incense; and place some powdered emplaster on top, either from strong or another type of plaster, and let it sit for a while until it starts to come out, then treat him with ointment until he is cured.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of sewing is that you assemble the seam: or by needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or by thread, as I told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips.
