A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	With the same hand it goes into the lips abscesses, like grains of wheat, small and large ones; therefore you must return to the lips, and cut each one apart, taking out with pincers and striking in each part; then apply later after the vitriol incision breaks, until the pus is stained; and then clean with water, and treat it for dry things until it becomes healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the gum of the teeth.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	In the work of this chapter, there are many times when you will see swollen gums with a lump that they call "albulus"; so it is fitting to hold them tight in tweezers, and cut at their root, and let the blood flow or the wound; then put vinegar or other powder on the wound, restricting and drying out; and if that one returns after the incision, and it happens many times, if you cut it again and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of ulcers to be removed.
des sordens	About ulcers.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	There are no cases where the teeth are assembled at the top of the gums in the mouth between the teeth, with rough and painful scabs; and there is also a black and yellow tooth with worms, until corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is foul-smelling. It is fitting that you seat the patient between your hands, and have his teeth held steady, and remove the teeth or scabs as soon as they appear; and apply various ointments such as vinegar, green, yellow, and other concoctions until they are smooth; and if one removes the tooth on the first attempt, it is good. But if not, then recurrence begins again on the second day and third day, until you have removed all of them; and learn that teeth need various forms of ulcers to be removed, according to what the work shows, because those who shave off the teeth that are extracted between the gums have other forms than those who shave off the teeth.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you delay no longer than until you can get it treated, because this should not be done by anyone; because it is a very high substance, therefore there is no excuse for delaying the treatment.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to receive treatment, it is necessary that you are certain of the feeling in your tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain of the patient is mistaken for tooth decay, and it thinks that this is the good tooth, and treats the healthy tooth; and sees no way to escape the pain because of bad tooth structure, because we have not wanted to do so with these healers; and when you are certain about feeling in your tooth, it is necessary that you scorch around the tooth at all angles strongly to ward off the gums of all parts; then remove the molar to your two teeth or with fine pliers at first, as much as possible until they are well cleaned up, then firmly fix the pliers; and place the patient's jaws between yours, and his good tooth so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extractions, pull the tooth directly towards the fracture, and if it doesn't spring forth, take hold of one of these instruments and pour it inside each opening lightly, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is fractured and has become infected, it is fitting to fill in with cloth, where or at the perforation; and if one carefully ties a string around it, so that it does not break when tightening, it is necessary to be very careful over the gum to smooth out the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And beware well that you do not break it, and leave one part intact, and report to the patient about the pain in the root of the tooth, for greater pains are in the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not do this as the ignorant master who by his haste and bravery breaks a cart every time, and does not bring anyone to it but what we have told you; but sometimes they come upon it by the stomach of great disease because of the roots that remain, or because he breaks the cart, just as it has often happened; and when the tooth is weakened, wash the root in wine or vinegar or ash; and if bleeding comes, which often happens, then apply a root of vitriol broken; and if this does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the ulcers, when one pulls out the teeth first, are long points and big roots, which do not double when you pull out the tooth; and these are:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And are big members if they do not bend when pulled out, and are made of good iron, and have teeth to hold them.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root stays in place after pulling, it is advisable to put some cotton soaked in butter on the wound daily or twice.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the joint is mummified, put on the tongs called "algefry", because the head seems like a butcher's knife; and they are made just like a file, which is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to emerge from all these ties, so it is advisable that you uncover the skin completely around the root, and put the instrument which is called "althali", this means nail, because there is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is hard and great, and the root does not break, but jumps out of that, this is good; but if not, then assist with all the instruments, because the forms will come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one assists with this instrument which has two nails, then it is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are in front of the roots of the teeth, and this instrument which resembles a large pincers, with this shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And so this instrument is not to break, and he knows that many instruments of bones are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the skilled masters find by himself his own instrument, according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are two kinds of diseases out of these and the ancient ones do not teach a tool for each, because it breaks neither on stone nor on other bones, nor in any other place, but rather he seeks instruments that it is necessary, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, because this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well fitting to hold the bone, so that they do not slip, but can hold it and remove it; and then restore him with medicines suitable for this, and if he has putrotion in the bone, and it is small, if all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not to be according to their natural body form and their shape is ugly, and in young women as well, it is necessary that you know if the teeth are new after the tooth, and they are not in the right place, and you cannot fix or limit them: therefore take the saw; and if it is a bit with the tooth, take this instrument with the form shown here, which is like a small beak, and is made of iron with good quality.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the saw cuts and cuts every day in order to make the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that we can fix it, then take a thin nail with the shape shown here.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also as with the nail, when we make nails; and in cutting the tooth cut and cut every day gently, so that it does not move until it chips; then the plane is finished at the end without any sharp edge, and if the teeth are too pointed and they chip the tongue, it is necessary to file the roughness so that it becomes even, so that it does not chip the tongue nor corrupt the voice.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth are loose, either by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot press down on it so that it does not hurt, and you have cured them with medicines restraining them, and this is useless; if they need to be restrained, use a thread of gold, because silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never moves; and if the wires are too fine or too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth move, take the thread and tie it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the pins between the teeth of yours, if there are one or more, until you see straightening gently from the sound of the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume the covering just where you started, and carefully and skillfully, so that it does not move at all; and if your tie is loose to the root of the tooth so that it can escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Instruct the patient to hold the head of the shoulder with a pair of tongs, and assemble them, and put it between two healthy teeth, and so that the tongue does not hit; then let it stay as tight as you can, until it loosens or the thread breaks, if it stays on, tie it with another thread; if it stays and serves, do so for its entire length, and this is the form of the bone and the shape of the alignment of two healthy teeth, and two unhealthy ones, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, fresh to fresh, just as we have said; and do not let anyone touch it who is not learned and skilled, for no one has ever done this shape of a tooth of bone, and put it back in place where it is defective, and tie it so as we have said, and let it stay there until it serves, for its entire length.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Close the bandage around the neck
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never cut the ligature of the tongue which comes from under the tongue or naturally, for it will happen so. Or by accident of a wound that has been sewn. And such wounds are such that you work on the mouth of the patient, and keep your hand in the healthy one, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve ligament near the large vein, until the tongue is loosened from its place, and if there's any hardness or knot, and it's caused by a sudden wound, so pour some wine into him and cut near the large vein that one. And beware that the tear is not too deep in length, lest the artery be injured; and when you have done this, lift the patient to lukewarm water and asyls, or cold water; then put under the tongue a linen bandage.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If they bleed from the wound comes, then put vinegar on it and break with the glass; and if it does not stop, then cauterize with slow cautery, which is good for those; then treat with other treatment until he is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pus is seen in color, whether white or black or hard, and if the patient does not feel it, and you do not touch it at all, because it's a chancre; and if he inclines to bleeding, and there is moisture, then remove the tumor, and make the wound with a fine brush, and deliver from one side and from the other; and if it does not stop bleeding to its own work, put vinegar on it and break with glass until it is stained, then return to its own work until you have treated all thoroughly; then lift the leg with ease and security, and treat with other cures until he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Blood from the neck.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	There is no occasion for the neck pouches called "godath", and we call them simply two pimples. When you cure them, as we have said in division, they will be healthy, but if it's a hard spot with small hairs and flesh color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is big, do not touch it with iron, for the same reason of blood; but let it remain until it is dead, and then you will cut it out, or it would break apart by itself. But if it has a pale color and small roots, cover it with an instrument, but first examine whether the abscesses are closed and have subsided.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then set the patient against the sun, and have their joints be sound, and work on their mouth and press the servant between their hands, and push the tongue under all the instrument, so that this is the form; and it shall be of silver or fine gold just like our scales:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue to all this instrument, and see the abscess, if take one pinch and insert it into the almond, and draw it out above what you can; and draw none of the threads with it, then cut at the instrument, so that here is the form, which looks like force; and view the head are curved, and one place another, and are very good, and it's made of iron or wood or linen:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument, then cut with tongs, so that here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	Et doit être touched from one side and the other side; and when you have cut one of the walnuts, so cut the other in the same manner; and after the incision gargle the patient with hot and cold water, and with a mixture of blood, or green pomegranate rinds are cooked, or myrtle flowers, and similar things, until they stop bleeding; then the cure will continue until the patient is healed; and once there are other abscesses in the throat besides the two walnuts, cut them accordingly as the two walnuts are tied.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was nestled in the throat, which is to say the little abscess; and I had closed her throat very tight so that the patient could not breathe through the obstructed passage, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if she had stayed like that for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses are made so high that they have been placed two times by two entrances in the flesh.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore applied at once, and put in one of the incisions, then made two cuts with a knife, and took off a great portion of bowel; then I put another incision in the other entrance in the flesh, and held his jaw shut and pressed his tongue; after that I put in an incision into these abscesses, and cut away a part, and from it came out only a small amount of blood; and thus I stopped the bleeding from the neck of the woman, and now she began to drink cool water and then wine, and did not stop cutting at that abscess for a long time; the abscess kept recurring, and filled up the wound that I had made empty, until it became very large; therefore I closed it and cauterized inside the throat: thus he remained still as he grew; and I left those parts, and only God knows what came of them after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the eye falls and is prolapsed and grows long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cut as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the swelling of the abscess has subsided, and it is subtle, then it is advisable to copy it; and that which is rounded and is not long; and if it is sanguine or has a red color or black, it is advisable to avoid making another incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner as I have said, its size and shape, seat the patient in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument we remembered previously; then insert the needle into the eye, and pull outwards, and cut at the second and third instruments as we mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is fitting that you not cover my forehead more than the natural surplus; for if you do so, it will grieve your voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the two almonds, and heal as much as possible until she is cured.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of cutting, it is fitting that you use a needle at the cautery of their fearful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of cautery is water and aqua.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient puts their head on your healthy one, and then presses their tongue with the instrument we have mentioned in the cautery chapter, and mixes it with hot water vinegar, if it is neither too thick nor too clear; and uses the upper part of this instrument, for this is its form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to put a hair or an ointment on the head as they like, with a spoon's help, and place the instrument under the medicine so it runs into the mouth from there; if it comes out to the throat instead, let the saliva and mucus flow, so that it doesn't land in the neck, then take hold of the instrument and press it against the forehead until you see its color change and the mouthwashes of the medicine are calmed down; if you see this, pick cotton and tie it on any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and pour the instrument into the cotton bag, so that the cotton is soaked under the forehead; do this often, till the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and cut off after four days or five; if you need to renew the application of the medicine, do it again, and after the cautery wash it with cotton in front of the forehead, with lard and butter, and clean what's around the medicine.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take camphor and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and avranne and similar herbs, and mix all of them together in a pot, and then put them in a vessel, and boil it; and let the pots be well sealed with strong earth, and add to each pot an instrument according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And so it should be made of silver or lead, and put a bone into the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises up to the eye through the nose, until the eye is numbed; after that, repeat it often, until the eye dries out, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the aposteme's heat, because many things happen; and do not do this except when the aposteme is turning cold.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a knife and put it into the chief a small piece of metal, so that the mouth of the patient will have no more pain; for the piece of metal does not weigh down the vapor, which is good to set right the health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Sometimes it is said that the neck is swollen with or without an arrow of fish or any other thing; so it is therefore necessary to treat what you can see, and press the tongue on the sun until all the instrument, so that you see the thing; and if it does not open up and returns to the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit also when the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it irritates the arrow further with vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of bread, or a root of lettuce, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie it with a thread to the sponge, and then apply glue; and when it comes loose, you will pull it out; and if it does not come loose from what we have said, take an instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Instruct the patient to let the curved instruments pass through the throat so that they can enter more easily, and raise the head high, so that you do not touch the epiglottis; for if you touch it, the whole thing will come alive, and do not push the bone in; instead, make sure the patient pushes out with the instrument, because he must push or pull to get it through, since it is curved on both sides; so that when pushing, either the instrument goes down, or they have to treat the entire instrument equally, until it is pushed through.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat's curvature
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the curvature of the throat treated, as I said in division, by the treatment of medicines; and if it does not help, then look at the patient's throat in front of them, in the sun, because you should press their tongue against the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the poultice, so it has a single thread or fine needles that are worth.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this is not worth anything, take a single hair of the patient's body and put it into the poultice, then pour or sprinkle hot wine on the foot.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is constantly vomiting water.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water and open the mouth, let it be swallowed in the direction that is easy to swallow, and move (the poultice) with your hand frequently; and as soon as the patient feels the cold water, he will vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not vomit as we have said, then suffumigate the patient with asafoetida, in the instrument that I told you to use for the fumigation of the wound; do this many times, because she will vomit with a more bitter odor.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et the manner of fumigation is that you take an iron pot or one with charcoal vis, and cover it with a sieve pierced in the middle, and through this hole the joints of the instrument are; then put the patient’s head into the cage so that they do not smell the smoke, but only feel its heat, and now the ulcer will appear, and if it does not come out, repeat the fumigation several times; and let the patient suffer from thirst, eat unclean things and vomit, and drink no water; and thus they are cured by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument for treating the ulcer is such that when it can be seen, resembling curved tongs to insert into the throat; and has the appearance of a beak, and has roughness like lime, so that what touches it cannot pull away; and thus it is:
li chapistres des apostemes	The physicians of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many similar abscesses are found, according to what is remembered after one another in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two manners of doing it, one being the same as the other, because of moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those who are inside or on their body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Because the abscesses of the head are different from those of the breast, and the abscesses of the liver are different from those in the joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced, until the bowel is dead according to its completion; and for those of them who it is necessary to pierce when they are considered, and do not die according to their completion, as those abscesses near the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess comes from the joints and is left until it becomes putrid, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, because this is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is in the main limb, and if you delay the perforation until it dies, this will harm the principal member; or if it's near the foundation, if we pierce there as well, so that it dies; and it is not advisable to pierce an abscess when I believe digestion is completed, for fire, because what's in the foundation will rot from the inside out, and become a fistula; and cannot be healed in great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the sign of the perforation of the abscess which appears according to its completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of the fever, and the reduction of the pain and redness, and the gentleness in the movement and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation so as to be more dependent on its location near the abscess, and where it opens up; and let the perforation be made long in the body, if the abscesses are in hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and in those places equalized or where there is no pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these areas where they are swollen, by the order of that physician.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And if an abscess is in the groin, so that you should close the perforation until it has been fully digested, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	But if you pierce this area, the wound will become infected with the venom from it, and it is full of much filth, and perhaps the lips and surrounding tissue will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is in any area that needs to be pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the limb has need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	It is necessary to pierce small abscesses in small punctures, and large ones in large punctures, and many cuts according to the resemblance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses that it is advisable to cut the vein, and cover; when it has become as thin as a drapery, and has lost its strength, then it is advisable to do so as they make for the bulbs: and if there are such ones that are split into three angles, and those whose veins are pierced like the bee of myrtle, like abscesses from arrows; and if there are such ones where one makes a rounded punch, and other shapes and sizes of cuts, and like cutters.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, as an abscess is superficial, it is necessary to let them pierce entirely; and when the abscess is large and has collected great bile, and you pierce, so that you do not take all of the bile in this hour, but only take part of it; then stop the abscess just after the other day, then take away no further; do this many times until the entire bile is taken; meanwhile if the patient is weak or an old man, a pregnant woman, a sick child, or an old man decrepit with age.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	But if they wait for the outcome with no hope at all, in case the patient dies, and you do not rejoice.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound opens, and examine whether the wounds of the abscess are small; and if it's a clean cut, apply tourniquets made of linen or old cotton; and if it's a large abscess, and there is much damage, it's necessary to insert tenters in each one so that they come together when wet; and if you have pierced an abscess with a part of the skin and wrapped it around, it's necessary to fill it with old cloth or rustle of linen with moisture, and tie it on the third day; then apply the treatment and care until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if they are bleeding from the wound, give them cold water and oil, and apply a dressing made of wool, and cover it with linen, as often as necessary.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they continue to bleed from the wound, give them a gentle remedy and treatment, and the powders in my hands that are in this book; and if it is winter time, and the wounds or abscesses are very nervous, so should you put on bandages and cloths moistened in wine and oil hot. And if it's dry, and the wound is charred, so should you put on moist cloths in water and oil, or in hot wine and oil, every three days, as we have said; and then remove the abscess and wash it clean and cure it, if it seems good to do so, until they are healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what it means to know thoroughly in the treatment of abscesses: or as we have said how one must go before treating an abscess, and here it is explained by the chapter.
des soros	of sorrows
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head of smallpox comes in little pimples, and there are many kinds of them, just like on linen, as well as the joints of a rabbit, and there are many of these similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and like those that are moist as flesh; and there are also some that are hard and rocky to cut, and there is no doubt if the arteries are not affected.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the signs of swelling at the waist if you have tried all instruments that are called "inter-mixable", because the form comes after this, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then they fix it at the top of long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is empty, then they scrape without leaving any of that skin that contains the moisture, because it returns to its place when they leave nothing there; then plunge cotton in ointment Egyptian, if present; otherwise, in water and wool, and apply the wound, and let it remain till the next day; and those who have stayed through the night will be corrected.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then reapply the cotton, as before, on the second day, and apply ointment to the wound until it is clear that it will not stay through the night; then cure the wound with ointment suitable for its condition, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscesses hold fast and stick to the bone, apply according to this form, from top to bottom; scrape your incisions all around, and put all your treatment under the cloth where it is; and if the arteries cause contractions, do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And so do as I have said about the abscess if it is pierced, and with the cutting and with curing just as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting on the pierced abscess and the moisture, if it is lighter, because there is less blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or heads are without any moisture, and such as I copied or observed in an old woman's head; and I found the abscess just like a hard, rough, and white stone that cannot be broken; and if anyone had been burned by one, it was done just as if they had been struck with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come or heads, wherever these come on the child's head and on their ear roots, cut so that it is always as far back as possible, to make the bowels come out; and treat as is necessary.
des scrophules	diseases of the skin
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often they happen on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come out elsewhere or in the body, and are very strong, and are joined together one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly inside its own side, just as the lump and the abscess of the head, just as we have said; and there are many similar scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are also malignant ones that refuse to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one then, where you see a person with good disposition at the throat, and is similar to the color of the body, and is mute in all parts and does not have any inflammation at the neck or artery or conduit, and is not deep; it is therefore fitting to copy it from above, and to scrape off each part, and they will be the two lips red like those that are near the eyes, if you need to do so, as we said in abscesses of the head; and make it a little bit at a time, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or vein, and should not touch too much before, that you do not cover what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	Instruct the patient to let the vein or artery bleed and do not stop it if blood does not come out, so pour vitriol into the wound, or apply some powder that stops the bleeding, and bind up the wound; and leave it until the abscess is closed, and the wound is softened, and begin to clean.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the head is not scarred, it returns to its place as long as you complete what you started; then seek an expert's advice if there are no small swellings remaining, so that you cut and lance them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	If there is a great vein at the root of the swelling, it is not advisable to cut that vein only at its root, but tie off the head with a strong double thread and let it fall down without disturbance; then apply cotton wool soaked in Egyptian ointment to the wound.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cover the entire scrofula, it is fitting that you assemble the two lips of the wound and sew them now, so there will be no remaining swelling from the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is fitting that you cut off the root of it, and treat the furrow, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have swelling, make a puncture in the place where it opens and bleeds; and make the puncture as described earlier, depending on it, then apply ointments with and similar things, so that the corruption does not remain after it has decayed; and when the wound is well cleansed, if ointment applied to it will bring healing, until it is cured.
de squinance	of supination
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient men spoke and said about the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and that is what their words wrote.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	To those who have supinated, it is necessary to avoid cutting the throat called "epiglottis"; and do not give aid by that, because all the veins and the flesh of the sick are those that have inflammation in the mouth, or in the throat or in both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the canal of the flesh, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it under three circles or four a small cut across, between two circles or by the quantity of the incision across the septum, not in the cartilage; and this way, it is most suitable to the section of the epiglottis, for there is no cartilage left, and the tissue is long to be reached.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	Instruct the master to stretch the skin of the neck to its entirety if they are fearful; then cut the vein until it comes to the point where the blood begins to flow; and escape the vessels of blood, if you see any thing; and then strike the vein, as we have said; and demonstrate by section of the throat's vein that sprang from the broken limb, and by the failure of the voice; and leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and one doubts strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound on the vein, and pluck out the whole skin up to the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	But do not do this just because the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the disease has made them weak.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Adonques cope on the epiglote because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and so the ancients commanded to leave the wound open for as long as the sickness of the disease passes, and it has passed in three days or four days. And then they ordered to sew up the wound and cure, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut off part of the navel cord; and I was called to cure her, and found her also dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood that was coming out of it, and I realized she had not cut herself in the vein or by force just to the throat, but the blood came out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I have failed to translate the text line by line into English.
de la grosse gorge	from the big throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	The cistapstance (abscess) is called a "thorn in the throat", and it's a large abscess of a color like blackberry, and it occurs especially in women; and there are two kinds: one by nature, and another by accident. For if it occurs by nature, it has no ulceration.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to two kinds: because one is similar to fat flesh, and the other is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and it's feared, and it shouldn't be treated with hot fire, only in those who are small and thin, and you should search for it near the beginning of the opening. If you find it as if it were fat flesh, but there is no vein, and you can't find a cause, then cut it like one cuts meat, and remove all its covering, if there's nothing left; and make sure to search thoroughly, and cure it so that it becomes completely healthy.
des nous	it commands
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways to cut us, in which I will say all the similarities; and it is necessary that I tell you the difference between cutting and piercing.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that piercing is then and fever stays, as long as the ebullitions are not passed, and until the putrefaction is completed; therefore, rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With piercing there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains the syphilitic, which is its own sac and takes on the colour of the flesh, and begins to swell like an apple, and becomes big; and are thus similar or in proportion to the size, or moisture, or colour, as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treatment with new things, that you first test and inquire about all the instrument called "entremoissoire", according to its form or chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses from us is that you pierce or suck out as much moisture from them as you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then remove the "entremissoire" and be careful not to force.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the abscess bursts and its color is such that it resembles a certain thing as I have said of other abscesses; and if after removing the "entremissoire" there is no more moisture, then know that it is fat, so make a cross with it, and take hold with your fingers, and lightly shave each part and guard the side where you are treating it to be made sound with the nose; and if you cannot treat it sound, then tear it apart piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it stays there, then the joint comes back to its place many times; and if it remains for just a little while, without causing any harm, apply the wound with some corrosive powder, hold the wound tight, and put on soothing things at the abscess site, and cure other wounds until the patient is healthy; and if the joint becomes large, cut off two fingers of the wound, and cure the one who causes inflammation to that spot.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is beaten against you, or some other cause, hasten and apply the left (of) vitriol broken, letting it sit for two days or three, until the wound opens up, and rests in the boiling of the blood; then return to cover what is left.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the entombed strumens, and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small; and among them, there are three quarters called "albaret", and one called "breb"; and also they have three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistulas; and are also like the needles used to sew suture, and are made of citrin (gold), iron, or silver, and move in a way that makes them yellow, and are more useful for puncturing black pus to encircle the corbuses (abscesses) of fistulas; and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the perforation.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of ulcers are much like appearances, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and those with two corneas in three manners also; and those with three corneas, and are in three manners; and those with two corneas, and a single cornea alone, and are in three manners; and all these are necessary for their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these is cut to be sharp, and of such are those who do not cut from both sides, because of the scorching of the nerves, so that one does not cut the vein or the nerve; and these incisions cause the painless response in hands, so that the patient does not lose anything at the opening of the abscesses; and they come in three manners: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one should use none more than what is needed for a chariot, such as legs, arms, and fingers, and similar limbs; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling scabbards of fistulae, according to this form, so that they stain the vein.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and he puts him back at no time into the place where he had previously bled and cut veins, and arteries, and at no time returns to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never do the breasts of any men swell when they begin to rot, as much as they resemble those of a woman; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wishes to cure them, should wait according to this form, from the line a. to g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and apply a poultice of medicine to the wound, using char, then assemble the two lips of the wound with stitches, and treat until it is healed; and if the breast swells down, and becomes tender as in women, so that one closes over another at the end of each, as these wounds do, where one stays attached to the other at the end of both, so that the greater line contains the lesser according to this form, from the line b to g; then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powder, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision has not been fully made, because the sick person does not wish to rest, or for the drying up of blood, so that you fill the wound with wet cotton cloth and corrosive ointment; and leave it until the swelling subsides and the fat remains, then treat until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Blood from an abscess.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	When abscesses come from under the armpits are hard sores or with boils, and if there is moisture in them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture therefore must be cut according to this form, from the line .b. just above the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire bowel that is in the abscess is empty, apply a dressing of old linen to the wound, and let it stay there for another day, then remove all the linen, and treat with ointment fitting to these so long as it becomes sound.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are like boils, treat them as we have said in cutting boils, and if the wound is to the bowel, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	About the cutting of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut, and the skin is sewn over it which is above, if there are many abscesses; and just as there are in the vein if it bleeds and an abscess; and if one knows such a time when it's for the artery, then the abscesses will form long and deep into; and when you feel with your hands, you'll feel strangulation; and when it's for the vein, you'll know that there is no pulse; it's madness to cover this abscess, and even more so when it's below the armpits and navel and at the throat and in many other places, and it's very large.
