Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to stop the iron treatment, and one who has a head injury should also do so, and in one who is swollen from an artery cut under the skin, make incisions above the skin at the long point; then close the waist with stitches, and carefully remove the artery from the tissues, until it is uncovered; then insert an arrow into the wound on the opposite side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in extracting two arteries in the temples; then keep the patient who has no pulse tied up until there is one, and treat the abscesses accordingly until he is healed; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, it is necessary to cut out all the skin from the abscess with an arrow, then cut the surrounding swelling and leave what is tied; then put on a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, and keep treating tenths and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	Out of the abscesses of the flesh.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	This occurs when abscesses come into the artery and vein, or they form on the skin when it is inflamed, or due to excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the joints and the tendons where there are no bones, it's an abscess that causes grief, and its color seems like the color of the flesh, and is associated with more severe dispositions and pain; when they strain and cut, the patient feels pain, but not from the bone itself, rather from below the joint; and they remain still in all directions, neither moving forward nor backward, nor above or below, and one who has joints should not be covered with iron: by chance it may cause contraction; and those who are on their head or forehead make the skin swell.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if you have tweezers and cut it in its root; and if it's large, if you suspend it to a thorn and scrape it clean, then skin and sew up the wound to the spine, and let the cure be until he is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	of large boils hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There is never any occurrence in the intestines and no other part of the body that can be compared to it, and this illness is called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and has subtle roots and large boils; and there are both small and very large ones; I saw one man who had two bellies that were almost like fungi in shape, with no difference whatsoever, and they were white, and had a small root, and had been split open, and were rotting away due to moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	Instruments were copied and I found one weighing 18 ounces, and the other 6 ounces, and the wounds in the incision are such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the navel is white and moist with a subtle root; if you cut to the spatula wide, and be present before you apply the cautery to fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	But when cutting comes many times too great bleeding from the incision, and if you do not hold back, then hasten to the cauterizer; and if you see the patient fearful and afraid of the incision with fire, take a well-made ligature, and tie the navel as we have said, and let it be for two days; and then bind it, and stop tightening the ligature until the ligature cuts the navel, feeling by its presence; and if the roots are large, fear to cut myself in the abdomen, but you can well cover half of it, then cauterize so that it does not come back; then treat the wound, and guard that you do not cover the part that is of a foul color and poor smell and yellow discharge.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	This is an enchantment of an ulcer, and I have come to this cure after it.
quant li boude ist fuer	how the boil swells
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	When the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or a cut in the sac, and is on the abdomen and there are some boils, just as it happens in other types of wounds, or when a vein or artery bursts according to what is in front, or due to heat from venous or arterial cuts; and if this is by the wound of the syfac and by the issue of the boil, then its color resembles that of the body, and is a light thing accompanied by pain, and opens up through various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is through the intestines, then it is more diverse; and when you press on its two sides so that it recurs, and then returns, and by chance it becomes hard, and enlarges greatly at the entrance of the bath and for great work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	Et se c'est pour moistor, c'est legiere chose, 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It must be left to heal.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or gall bladder, you must command the patient to fast and stretch out straight, then stifle all noise around the belly; then command him to rest between your hands, then go into the place where you have marked with a broad bandage; then cut the quarter of the abscess up towards the top at every inch; then tie it tightly with a strong rope or a cord of fine silk firmly, and bind it with no space allowed; then operate on the quarter of the abscess stretched out over the bandage, and pour your bile into the intestine; if you find the bowels bound by the thread, release them, and pour the intestine into the opposite side of the belly; and if you find the gall bladder, cut it at its joint, and cut away superfluity; and if the vein is against it or the vein, go skillfully to it, then return to your work and take 2 sharp needles, and pour 2 strong threads through them, and put the two needles into the place where you have made a puncture; then strain the abscess in 4 places above the threads, and if you see, remove the threads, and let the patient rest until he is able to pass; and tie off the charred parts with himself; or cut it when it has passed subtly and quietly, then perform the cure as we have said; and take out the suture or moisture that you find, then cure the patient as they need, and heal the skin.
dou chancre	A chancre (or canker)
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division that the symptoms of a chancre are similar to those of cancer, and how one must treat it with medicines, and how one should avoid using iron treatment; and we say that chancre is found in the milk (or breast), and great care must be taken when treating it; and the ancients said that when chancre is present on someone, or if it can be removed like a chancre from the nipple, or when it appears similar to other places like the udder, then one should remove all of it at the beginning; but when it grows large and old, it's not advisable to approach it, because I have never found anyone cured by it; nor has any one ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the wounds, when it can be removed from one's body, as we have said, is that you should purge the patient of black bile once; then make them healthy if they show signs of repletion; then make the patient good to heal; then put on your poultices or chancre, and the head of all parts, and leave nothing remaining in any part; and let the wound heal fully, and expect well the recovery with one's hand, or with anything; but if the blood flows from the wound and causes contrariety to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize as much as possible so that it is not left stained; then cure with another treatment until they are healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	For we have said in the division of these diseases (idropisie), and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each one of them, and the cure that is made by medicines, and the one that is cured with iron: since it has been exposed; and you should not touch iron in these two similarities: I mean tympanites and yposarche, because this is a deadly thing; therefore when you give medicine to this similarity of idropisie called "exclites" by medicines, and the cure does not profit, look at whether the patient is weak, or if he has another disease than idropisie, just like fever and solution of belly and similar things; do not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient very weak, and he has only idropisie alone, and his limbs are neither too old nor too new, then do thus: lift up the patient straight with your hands, and the minister presses the belly towards the lowest part of the thigh, then take the spatula with an iron spine according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let him cut with two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Cut with a point and be careful not to enter too far so that it doesn't come out into the intestine when you insert it, and can't be pulled back; then examine if the abscess is attached to the intestines: if it's suitable to cut through under the bone on the outer side of the third vertebra above the joint; and if the abscess is for liver disease, if so it should be made on the left side of the third vertebra; and if it's for the spleen, if so it should be made on the right side; but it's not advisable to have the patient lie on the cut side so that the swelling doesn't run into the weak part. Then pierce all around with the instrument and push it in, and hold your hand tight over the entire strap between the skin and the sac as if you're scraping away to the length of a finger or until it comes out; then pierce the sac until the strap reaches eight, and that's the measure of water, then pull it back, and pour this instrument from which it is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it seems like a silver knife, and is made of iron or of a lightweight wood, and has a small defect in that place; and on one side there are three cuts, and two on the other side, and one more so; and the head of the knife is cut as fine as a feather, and this is the shape of the incision which the scribes make with the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	The blood vessels on the surface are cut off, so when the instruments come to the water, they now flow upwards onto the instrument; drain it then, for if you drain more than is fitting for that hour, by chance he may die from the resolution of his spirit in the weapon, or he loses his hands, or he approaches death; but drain according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the disposition of the virtues signifies in the sick person's body, and his feet; then take out the instrument and hold back the water, for now it is held by the clot that covers the cut on the skin, which is why I said to pierce according to this method; then resume the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering from that, and draw off a small quantity of water; do not do this every day, and beware of making fools of yourself until it does not last but for a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant. de la circoncision	About circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut. The ancient ones did not tell about circumcision of their children because they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we acquired by experience.

de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I said the difference between the stone that is hard as rain, and all the signs, and for which stone one must cut or work out size; and on the bladder, and on the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone in the bladder which is hard like the earth is most often found in children, and it's a sign that the water has jumped out of the bladder like water in its subtlety; and they open the vein, and scrape the patient's penis, and pierce them many times, and then swell; and because of this jump many have fallen to death; and the healing is lighter in children until they are four years old, and it's very painful in elderly people, and is more serious between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone, than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to clean the patient by cleaning, in order to draw out all the blood that is within his belly.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	Because it cannot be drawn out at any time.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by hand and feet, and push downward and move away, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and does not sometimes come up into him; then make him sit between your hands, and his hands should be below his knees, so that the bladder is completely relaxed downwards; then search for it and touch within; if you feel the stone in the space, immediately cut now on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out through the touchstone at all, moisten your right index finger with oil from your left hand, because if the patient is sick or has fever in his left side, and if he is young man having reached maturity; and put it into its fundament, search for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, push onto the neck of the bladder; then press strongly onto the spot where you see cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and he is commanded to stretch out his right hand to grasp the bones in the upper part, and his left hand to pull up the skin that is under the bones in the place where they make an incision; then he will pour the spatumile while it takes shape: for this is its form
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And put the one between the bones and the foundation, not in the middle but on the side of the left pig's snout; and straight above the stone, so that his two parts are adjacent to or meet with the foundation, and make a hole through it if it is wide enough by chance, otherwise narrow, according to the size of the stone, neither too large; for by accident the press may dislodge one of the bones in the foundation, which will fall into the work; and notice that there are pieces of stone or angles and margins: if it has a rough edge to emerge from; and if there is part that is above, like a nail, smooth, and rounded, whose emergence is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	In order to be free from angles and margins, do the following: make the incision larger; and if it does not bleed, so that you can strain the joint with the nails as sharp as a file on the head, in order to break the bone so it does not heal; or you put an instrument with a curved end under the head; and if you cannot do it this way, so that the wound is enlarged by splitting open the peritoneum, and if it has no opening, strain it with vinegar; and if there are more than one joint, first strike the largest one on the neck of the bladder, then make cuts upwards, then pull them out, and then cut the smaller ones afterwards.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, so that you can sew, and make a larger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For these two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes out again because the stitches cannot hold; but you must try with all your might to tie it up, or to cut off the nails, until you can bring it back in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with myrrh and aloe and dragon's blood, and tighten it, and cover it with a wet cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to calm down the inflamed abscess; then revive the patient on his back, and do not release the tie for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, apply a lot of oil and water well to the area, then treat with binding and dressing using powdered sulfur and powdered basil, until it is safe.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess comes to the wound and causes corrosion, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and it is retained there because of this, causing retention of urine, which is done in a certain way so that it does not flow with urine: put then your finger in the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains there, the bladder will corrode, and it will spoil; then lift the wound up with water and salt and cloth, and help him in all the ways you know, until he is safe; and it is to be considered that all the other treatments you give him should tie together the two legs, and assemble the medicines on the wounded area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the stone is small and it is embedded in the spine and fixed with a splint and the urine cannot come out; then so that I say again, if you cut off many limbs for this cure, you are excused from cutting them.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already experienced it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Put iron according to this form and fix them at three angles in one joint:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie it around the spine of the bone, so that it cannot come out again in the bladder; then put the iron in the vertebra lightly, until it comes to the bone; and turn the iron slowly towards the bone little by little, until you can pierce the bone from the other side; if soon after comes the urine, then press your hand on the part that is remaining of the bone which is inside the spine.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is so broken, and the urine falls with him, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents you, then tie a bandage under the bone and another above, then straighten the joint between the two joints, then pull it forth, and free the bandage, and clean the wound by means of ice which is in the wound; and care for the patient until he is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stones in women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There is rarely a stone found in women, and if it happens, the cure is painful, and is prevented by three things: one is that perhaps the woman may be virgin; and the second is that we cannot find a woman skilled enough to expose herself before mirrors, especially when she is cast out.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et the third method is that by chance one may not find a woman well-versed in this art of hands; and the fourth method is that the femur of the woman is more brittle than the femur of the man, because it can be broken with greater depth, and great fear comes to it. And if necessity requires such a thing, then it suits you to take a wise woman well-versed in life, and at pains go to her, and if you do not find one, do not choose a subtle woman; and let the present one show you a path well-versed in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to make that which you command from the inquiry of the femur; and look very carefully whether the woman is a virgin: then it suits you to break your vow at its foundation and search for the femur; and if she finds it, she will bind with a tie under her vow, and command you to pour your vow into or beneath the malaide, and to kiss and press her left hand upon the belly in form.

si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you feel the similarities to know the outcome.

de hernie carnouse	of a meatball hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	There is no other term for "ramice aquouse" than a mixture of moisture or white pus, which is below the clear part of the semen, and contains the yolk; it is called "syfac", and never occurs in the true semen itself, if one thinks it's another thing; and this happens because of the skin of the semen between the white syfac that we have said, and it is not.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this pus is weak that comes to the semen, and it spreads that material.

de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the joints
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	That in the cutting of this limb there is fear for many dispositions, so it seems to me that one should leave it; and I will tell you about the work and the similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that most abscesses come from the body, and equally from the joints; and it's a very common case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known that abscesses come from superfluous hot and cold, which spreads to the joints through percussion; and the colour of the abscess follows the colour of the body; it does not cause pain, but is an abscess in itself; and sometimes there are grievous and painful abscesses with hard and bloody color, and sometimes they come from a new artery or from inflammation in the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is caused by no artery, so it is found by the shape of an abscess, when you press on it with your two hands; and it does not happen to touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	That one which is caused by an accumulation of blood is found by its shape at the point of touch with your two hands, and it can be easily measured on this resemblance, and on other swellings; and you must cut to the vein, then stretch up the wound in the middle, and strip the suspensory ligament from all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the wound is already swollen with these swellings, it then seems that you must treat the wound and cut into it; and if there are veins on the surface, or inside the vessels, it seems necessary to deliver all those places and cut around them.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the arm is behind them, so it is fitting that you copy it entirely, and pull out the vein, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your wounds are completed, apply the dressing of woolen cloth moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat with other treatments until they are healthy.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses in the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess that has come out through a swelling similar to the groin area, with the softening of the joints, and the patient suffers greatly as it worsens; and the treatment for this illness is quite close to what was done before, and we will tell you about it, according to how the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	Instruct the patient to place himself on the elevated table, then pull the suspender cord over his head down to his toes, and cover all the nearby vessels with linen, and stretch them tightly; then cut at the spatumile trenching across the bone directly towards the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in extracting arteries that are in temples; then put a double thread needle into it where the vein enters, and tie it to the first part of the head where the vein is coming out, and tie off behind to the other part of the head; then cut straightly down the middle, according to the length of the body, and take out the corrupted moistures; then cure the wound as in others or if a vessel breaks, so that not one of the vessels is left uncovered; for by this there comes no harm, and all the vessels come back to life, so it is fitting to treat the vessels on all sides; lest the vein loses its movement due to the incision of the vessels, and does not heal.
de la routure dou syfac	of the cutting with the scalpel
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The symptoms of this infirmity are caused by the section that occurs as a result of cutting with the scalpel, or the extension on the belly in the region of the liver, because the intestines fall down from that cut to one of the joints; and this cut is either through the cutting itself, or the extension of it, and there are two kinds of cause: either from percussion, from a blow, from fire, or from lifting a grievous pain, and by similar things; and the signs when there is an extension of the scalpel wound, are that he has little by little for a long time, and does not come suddenly, and the abscesses equal in size until they reach the very end, because the cutting presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when there is a section of the scalpel wound that brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear diverse appearances under the skin, near the flesh, and it is because of the issue of the intestine and the body through the scalpel.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes it is bound to the ribs with the intestines, and held in place while, and the patient suffers great pain, especially when he is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And for these iron cauterizations due to fear, because it is so feared.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And in this treatment with iron, because it is so feared, you command the patient to bring his intestines into the wound if they can enter; then sew under his chin between your fingers, and lift the ribs; then cut the skin around the joints until long enough; then pour inside the belly tubes according to what you have in need to open the wound, and so that these tubes can come out; then scorch the flesh that is underneath the skin of the joints, until the white flesh is visible from all parts; then put your two fingers into the tube which follows the joint, between the white flesh that is under the skin of the elbow, and between the second flesh, and depart that which is behind the elbow, and between the second flesh; and then pull with the right hand inside the tube of the joints, and lift the elbow towards your left hand, and command the minister to extend the elbow above, and untie that which is after the binding; if you find no point of the intestines in the white flesh or until long time, put it into the belly on the outside. Then take an awl with a string made of 4 threads, and pour it into the back part of the flesh, which is behind the skin of the joints; after the belly, then cut the hairs that appear from the strings, as long as you have 4 threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the flesh with a strong binding of 2 parts; then tie the tubes of the strings, and if no vassal (a person who sucks blood) can enter into it, so that the abscess does not come out; and put the binding according to the first binding long 2 fingers from there, and after these two bindings, leave the flesh which is underneath the skin of the joints with a knot of one bow. And then cut in the part under the skin of the joints, until you do not find any more flesh or hair, as we have said before; then insert soft wool soaked in oil into the wound, and put it inside, and insert the binding that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes they are cauterized with white syrup after we have said, due to doubt of the slowing down of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and let the thread stay with it until it chooses to come out; and if it delays at the hearth, so that it arises from hot water, and puts on what we have said, until it comes out; then cure the wound with another remedy, until he is perfectly sane.
de hernie carnouse	of a hairy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this herb there I have never found anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made in such a manner as the herb which is assembled with the vis, by this kind of tie that you tie the straps, after cutting above the neck, lightly to the underside; then cut inside me, and cure the abscess that opens, until the strap chokes; and cure so as we have said, until he is perfectly sane.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the hair, if it muffles and heals the wound, so that it becomes clean.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syphilitic is constrained and has no appearance in the wound, and the cautery is more moist in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin around the joints.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	It often softens the skin of the joints in some men, because the charlatans who are inside it soften the skin, and it is clear to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, to make the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin over the natural skin; then assemble the two lips together with a seam, and see whether you wish, cut through the seams first the softening of the skin at three seams or four tightly; then cut between the seams, and the cure is done as in other wounds, until he is healed, and it will close with the hair.
dou chastrement	The healing from the fire cautery
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	It seems to us that cautery is a law, and for this reason I would not like to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two purposes: one is that the physicians should know how to respond when asked about it, and what treatment it is; and the other, because we have often had need of cauterization from certain animals to assist us, just as from oxen, sheep, goats, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that cautery is done in two ways: by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one we make by attraction, we seat the patient in hot water as best we can, until the coagulation is softened and relaxed; then we grasp them with your hand, until they are returned to normal and you feel them no more.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	In the treatment of swelling: it is to be noted that you should shave the best part, and press the skin of the forehead with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and strike at each person until you have thoroughly shaved; and let any little wart remain on the warts; and this manner of cauterization is better than that made by attraction, because in attraction there remains by chance some thing of the skin, because of which the best part desires luxury; then cure the wound as it is healed.
des hermofrodites	For those with hermaphroditism.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodit is according to two kinds of home: one is that between the two sexes appears like the figure of a woman's nature, or he has hair, and at times there is no urination.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is just like for women, and it has a point at the same place as a stick and two points.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for the humors and fever is that you copy all the connected cavities, and treat it as other wounds; in the second method, people who have urination through their urethral opening do not have a cure.
de la tentigene	Of the ingrown toenail.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	An ingrown toenail is a jointed cavity on the natural part, until it is too ugly to see; and some women have one as large as their hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to paint the surplus of the ingrown toenail on your hand or finger, and cut it lightly; and do not dig too deeply, lest blood comes out and the cure fails, then you must treat with another treatment until it is cured; and for a third joint that comes to the mouth of the mare's intestine, and the nipple, and by chance it opens, and it is as like a cow, and therefore they call it "old cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you must copy it, just like we have said, and the treatment until she is healthy.
de erratique	of a mistake
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	When the nature of woman is not recognized, or her parts are lost, and it is by birth, or by accident through disease that happens to her, or by chance collision, or subtle syphilis, and is caused in the mouth, or on the cost, or underneath, whatever it may be; and she fails to conceive, and childbirth suffers, and by chance flowers may appear, and knowledge of this is found through examination of the urine.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If there are signs of obstruction in the passage, choose to examine either your left or right side.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is swollen from the subtil (tissue or area) and it is close to two livres (likely referring to the space between the thumb and index finger), so hurry, and apply thus: put your two fingers together, and the woman lie on her back, spread out her legs; then form the two livres like this, until the subtil swell stops, and the stitches come loose; then take lard (or fat) in oil, and put it on the wound, and tie the woman to her bed every day, so that she can not sew.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the subtil (tissue or area) is hard and thick, it is advisable to cut with the spatula similar to the leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stitches are of charnel (likely referring to a material made from animal intestine or sinew), then apply pressure with an oncin (a small cloth or gauze) and cut; and have the medicine in stains (antiseptic solutions) like camphor, dragon's blood, incense, mixed together with many other herbs; then bring a large poultice made of plonc (likely referring to a type of moss or plant), so that the wound does not heal; and thus apply it for a long time, and bring in a tent of dry linen; and cure with other treatments until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	When there is a pain in the marrow, if you want to cover it according to this manner, unless it has an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	But when the abscess is in the marrow, one should not touch fire.
des emorroides	for hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that do not usually happen, and when old hemorrhoids occur they become swollen; and we have said in the section on divisions the similarities of ulcers, and signs, and I will say here those which receive a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and the swelling occur when they are full in the marrow, and they do not show themselves by feeling, unless it is a cure with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the root of the mouth can be felt, those can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary to put the woman in a cold house, then stand over her with iron tongs, and strike at its roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, like dragon's balm and incense, and similar things; then pour her feet in a hot water for an hour, then put her in cold water; and when blood comes out, if it is good, place her on a concoction of sumac and pomegranate rind, gall, and similar things, and then sprinkle with flour, mix with honey and easily, and make her drink from it.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it is bleeding, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this happens, if the patient pricks at it with a needle on their skin and hurts themselves, then take linen, and apply the poultice in juice of plantain or juice of agrimony with wine vinegar, and let them dry on the wound.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, treat the wound with a dressing until it is healed; and if that which is called "albathir" becomes red, and resembles an angry chief, then cover it as I have said; and then continue to treat until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses from the marrow.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come from the marrow, such as canker, porous abscess, herpes, and scabies, and other various diseases that I have mentioned in this division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary then that I tell in this book the abscess that comes to the maris, which is not an abscess but one that swells like a bow; and if you see how it works with fire, look whether the abscesses are swollen at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red then you can see it.
