Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not admire the instrument before arranging it, because its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second tooth is retained in childhood, it is convenient that you command the patient to hold their tongue, and then pull it out with a cloth, and restrain your hands at the mouth and nose; and if they spit through this, well is.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If that does not work, then take the knife and cut or make a hole, and put herbs that may open the mouth of the patient, just as calming, rue, anise, camomile, cassialigne, and centaurry; whichever of these are cooked or soaked in water on fire; then put a pot or caustic substance on top of the knife, and the other cloth in the mouth of the patient, and press until the vapors come out from within the mouth; then pull it out, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the head of the shoulder comes to a standstill.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure and is not in fever, instruct the barber to moisten her left hand with oil of sesame or musk rosewater, and then pour it into nature, and request the bloodletting; and when she has found it, seize it and stretch it little by little straight away, so that the hairs do not catch on the extraction; but they should move lightly from right to left, and then tie; if she goes and takes it off.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the blood of the hair is straitened in the jaw, we have said to treat with vomiting and fumigation of herbs; and if she is free from all that we have said, then be cautious so you don't go mad while treating; but it is fitting that what is at the head of the hair you tie to the armpit of a woman, then cover with ointment tetrafarmacoun; pour some medicine, and put her back, and she will come out; but beware, when you pour so it comes out bad-smelling in the stomach and the head, and the patient becomes ill.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is true, then fumigation is appropriate here: none of the ancients have tried fumigation with cresson and dry figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used when fumigating a woman in the retention of flowers and at the second joint if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to be seen like a knife, and put the subtle head in the nature, and the joints wide on the fire; and so let the fumigation upon the coals, and the vermin until it is eaten away, and begins another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	But some children are born who have neither pierced the foundation, unless it has been stifled by a subtle cauterization: therefore it is necessary to put them in pain where they pierce that cauterized place at their due time, and not hurt them with a sharp instrument, and girdle the bandage so that it does not touch; then put on a linen moistened in wine and oil, then apply the ointment until they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will stop bleeding, so put in or cut a ligature of cloth, and let the hands rest, and let them be left until the fever has gone to bed in the chamber.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes comes this stoppage of bleeding suddenly from a wound or an abscess; if it's necessary to cover that sudden blood-letting: if it heals, as we have said about the ligature of cloth.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the bottom.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the fundament are swellings, and those that come from outside the fundament after being exposed for a while, or in the space of the two parts, if there is a fistula or multiple ones; and when that swelling becomes old, it becomes ulcerated, and covered with moist, whitish, or subtle scab, and sometimes these fistulas become perforated; and they are caused by what the patient coughs up or passes, and perhaps gets some of it into his mouth.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that occur in the bladder and near half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the thigh and beyond a little from the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And so it is found that the fistula persists in the fundament, and does not persist: and thus you pour your two indices or foundation, and insert a subtle needle of flax or iron into the fistula when there is tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has tortuosity, you insert a subtle tent of linen or horsehair until you feel the tent or the hair at your mouth; and if you do not feel it, and there is no purging, no venting, or vomiting, as we have said: such a thing does not pierce, but hasten to the cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when a fistula is cut across at the bladder or just across the urethra, so that it opens, and the urine flows out, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived to be occurring at the joint of the thigh, then try to come towards the limb; if there is no twisting and no discovery of the pain inside, then it seems that it will again bow and will not benefit from medicine or a stitch by rubbing; and in these cut fistulas, there is no cure except for work and foolishness of those who interfere with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one that is not cut and not old, there is the hope of health by iron, as I have proven, if the patient lies between your hands on their back; and lift up his legs to his thighs, and incline his thighs towards his belly; then pour a vessel of wine, or a poultice if it has twisting, until you know where the vein is coming from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in his chest, so you should put your two fingers there, if you feel then that he tries to pierce it; and whether discovered or you sense between your thumb the sac or the char, then learn that she is punctured; but do not work on it any further unless we can heal her.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is not possible to heal all who are cut, but it happens rarely; and the aid that we do, if it is a scalding with subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as was said; and put hot water in the fistula until it comes from the root; and do this two or three times until you know that these scars must be burned, which resemble an ostrich feather; and then the cure uses soft tents soaked in butter until those scars are healed, and then the cure applies binding with thread and sewing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If so healthy, this is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is so, there can be no health; and if he tries to thrust between, and does not pierce just at the root which is on the foundation, and has a covering thick of fat or flesh between his two parts, and you see the fistula at that place where the covering is red and bloody; if you cut from the beginning of the fistula, and pour away afterwards the contents, and then apply cautery, as long as it comes to the head of the covering; and he will be freed from the fistula, and cured.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he does not fall backwards, and presses between you and the wound, so that the cautery of fire or medicine is applied.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery, assemble two things: this is to know that the charring of these charred bones joined together, and the stretching of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure for swollen testicles in butter or in a wooden chest, until they are healed, and if the bones become arse-dried in the bowels; then cure the wound of sudden onanism with hard charcoal, and those dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	But when it is restored, if it is healed and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes just to the bottom of the joint and is isolated from the body, you put two pounds or a pound on top of it, and then inquire about that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the pulse, and it's between two pounds of tissue or bones, where it's close to piercing, if there is only blood on its surface and expectation, by the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize as we have said, or you cut just at the bottom, or if you can, you put tenterhooks and cure as first; and don't go too far into it, lest you cover up the place that holds its foundation, and come to a painful situation by chance desire; then the cure, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you will remove that covering and the mucus when they are pierced from underneath the foundation, or with tenterhooks or another instrument appointed; then make sure of the cauterized piece in the wound, so much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula away from the opposite side of the foundation: if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes a fistula is made in this way; and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it remains on the edge of the fundament of the skin above, if you take a thread that perceives at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put the thread on the right side, and I push the tent into it to the entire length of the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is hanging on the margin of the fundament within, then pull out the thread from that puncture, as if you push your two fingers into the ground; and take hold of the head of the thread, and assemble the two joints together, so that one is held to the other, and leaves one day or two; and restrain it at no time, until the threads cut these marks which are between them, and then treat the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not heal or close, then pierce it in all possible ways that you can, unless it is too swollen.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not to be done when the swelling is too great, and then treat, as we have said, until he is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the sparrow's spur when a fistula is made is very rough and has one part that cuts in, and another part that does not, therefore you should not cut where you do not need to cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	from hemorrhages.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhages are in two kinds: either they are inside the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and on the surface there is a vein, and there is one or more, and it protrudes from the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that protrude have little moisture, and on the surface there is a spot, and sometimes a little redness, and they have a different color of flesh.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is fitting to bandage the torso in this manner: take one thread, and put it through a needle, and then take the thread up over and pierce the needle on the other side, and turn the two joints with the thread below the needle, so that it is not too loose; and tie the thread tight, then untie the thread, and pull out the needle, and do this for all the others, and leave one to check for the overflowing of the wound; then put a moist cloth on the wound's foundation, either in rose oil or in cerote, and put it on the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then let him rest until he farts, and when he will be cut, if the treatment with binding and other treatments is done, so that he may be healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	When dry or wet skin
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It happens frequently to have sharp stones in the intestine, and by natural constraint, when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is fitting to reset to the point of a spatumile or at your nail the scab above, which does not let it moisten; then treat as long as it feels sound as you wish; and if it cannot feel sound, restart the scraping more strongly than before, until it heals out, and is scabby; then treat until it is healed.
dou fremit	do not tremble.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A wasp appearance is an unwonted mark upon the body, and goes deep in it; and sometimes the truth of it, and one feels just as dead from trembling, and comes to all the body, and more so on the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Instruct the patient to take a quill of a swan's feather or a strong goose feather, and place that quill on the wound, until the purple ring appears all around; then turn your hand so that you cover all the area around the quill, and put it in its entirety into the wound, and set the quill to its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this of a quill of thorn or iron according to this shape, and be subtle below and behind, above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Don't pierce, lest it hold to two things, and pressure And if you see, if you cauterize the quill, as it is before or in front of the cautery instrument.
de la forme dou clistere	of a hollow tube
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	In no case is an artery pierced with silver or an arrowhead, or melted lead or armor; and in no case are these small and large instruments used unless they are brought near to it.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore those that should be used in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the pierced artery whether small or large is observed to be wide, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a deviation or the belly is bound, as you see, and the artery is perceived to be inside, and it has one puncture on each side, and the belly is wrapped with medicine from an animal hide or parchment, and they are noticed to be all around small punctures, and between each puncture there is 1/10 of a space, then push with a strong thread, like a thick twisted rope, into these punctures, and fill them up; and when the medicine is inside, if it adheres to the instrument in front of a strong thread, then pierce again; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Instruct the patient that the medicine should not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with a mixture of oil or ointment or something similar, then pour it into the mouth lightly. Then have the minister press his two hands together until it is all gone, then remove the plaster, and lift up the patient's legs as much as possible, if the medicine comes out, so that the wound will heal as much as it can; and if he sleeps through one night completely, so is a great aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you plaster his belly in a disease of downward flow of the bowels, and the medicine hastens to come out, then he will recur as long as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the seat or abscess, so that the plaster is as subtle as for an infant; and this is the form of the subtle plaster where the skin is constrained:
des plaies	Injuries
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division how to treat injuries; or you will tell me the treatments for hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that injuries are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to which one or which injury is being made, and why they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Things are made by wounds caused by hitting with stone, and the cutting of a sword or knife, or with a lance or a club or a seat, or similar things; or what is done according to the type of body parts, since some wounds fall on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the stomach, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you about each wound, and begin with simple head wounds, because they will be remembered in that chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I'll translate the text line by line into English:
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient if they do not wish to heal, so that their flesh becomes thin and they drink no wine, nor eat pork; and place on the wound, if it is swollen with abscess, cotton wool soaked in rose oil alone, or vinegar solution; and if there is no abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it does not move by the air, powder, which I will tell you of later; and if they have moved it, then put on some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a sword cutting and similar, and the lips cannot assemble with stitches due to the state of the mouth, then stitch them together, just as I will tell you about wounds in the belly, with sutures.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is discovered to be on the bone, and it bleeds, and holds only for a short time, if it opens; then treat the wound with medicine, and sew it back with cord of leather, and instruct the patient to eat large meat dishes, just like broth and bread cooked, as well as fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotting leather, and it's not adhering to the bone, if you cut off all of it, and drain the pus, then treat the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, that cannot be stopped without medicine, then choose which one to stop, and if you find the artery loose, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and put on this powder which solder the flesh as well as it has been moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to take a pinch of powder thus: take cinders by a part; dragon's blood by two parts; live calcine by three parts, and mix finely, and apply the wound and tie it tightly, until it becomes well healed and joins all its bleeding; then bind it well, and let it go, unless it swells, for you do not withhold medicine until it is clean.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never use only calcine when you do not have the cinders and no blood of the dragon, but only the arrows have moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the arrows have moved the wound, at the same time it was open, then do not put this powder on it; but put some other ointments prepared, or made of flour of barley soaked in water and honey, until they form a poultice; then treat with other treatments until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, if you make fine pinches; and I will tell you here after the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the head wound.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound on the head comes and it is simple, if it does not have any difference between the two of them in terms of the head, but if the nerves or artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, then nothing else should be done but to let the cure, and not put anything to restrain it, because the night causes the nerves to retract; and putting anything on the wound does not help, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of the disease is in the brain, which is the uppermost part of the body; but if you use medicine, such as calomel melted in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and apply it again to the wound also in sweet water, and other minerals like this, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, then bind it with strips of cloth, then care for it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and he is head and full of pus, pierce it or make a smaller opening under it; and if the artery has been cut, then remove the wound to prevent bleeding, and apply lye, cauterize it properly, that is the treatment; and if the spine of the neck has been cut, or the nerves, then keep the conduit in place, because the flesh will come, so sew the wound under the neck, and touch only what is necessary, and according to his natural figure; and then tie him up immediately, and let him rest for a few days, then care for his wounds with ointments until he heals; and if the wound has caused an impression in the bone, then see; and if there are pieces of bone, remove all the infected ones, since you can’t keep them; and those that you can’t get rid of, leave as long as the wound is open, and becomes dry and clean again; and if the wound is fresh, apply powder as I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and a fistula, then the treatment is as I have said in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of arrow or sword wounds
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's an arrow or sword wound, and the wound is deep, if you look at the depth of the wound, then know that the wound is mortal; and if it's not deep, but fresh with its entire sanguine (blood), don't put powder on it immediately, nor bind it tightly by the wound except to press down into its full depth, and return to him, and let him sleep upon the wound three days, or four, or more; if there comes no spasm, nor malady of heart, nor any other signs of death; and when you see his bones disposed well again, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds of boils and other treatments until they are healed; and if it cannot heal or work again, observe to see if there is an abscess; if so, perform the treatment as necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it is simple or on the back, treat according to what is in front of you; if it is large, suture; and if it is small, use powder; and if it has been embedded in the bone and cut into pieces, as needed, remove the wound if there are remaining pieces; and if not, let the wound dry out if it will relieve the extraction; and for other wounds, make judgment according to other members as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	fall of the bowels
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I have a small wound and no bowel issues, so it's easy to treat, this is one of the two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it's cold, cut the part in this way: moisten with a sponge or a single piece of cloth soaked in water only, or heat it in water with vinegar and spices, until the inflammation subsides; and no time should be wasted, so that it can be freed from swelling; and sometimes do this with wine to restrain it, and it will become more calm.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the inflammation departing, if you moisten the intestine with water or boil and mash it, because that is a way to alleviate the entry of many things; and if it cannot enter, so make a little wound in the instrument with which you strike the hemorrhoids; and the first cure is calmer than the size, so that none should cut it unless there is great necessity, for it's the instruments to break: if you pierce inside in the chamber and do not cover it up, and look at this shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine bursts forth, if you reset it according to its natural form in its proper place, if you have power to do so, for this is most beneficial.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, it is most advisable to make the patient lie on his back, with his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen, then let the head and stomach be raised higher than the lower parts, and so when there is a rupture of the abdomen in either of the two parts, pay attention to what I say regarding large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, apply what is appropriate for the situation, then take in your hands a pitiful minister who holds the entire rupture in his hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common way of suture, that you prick with an needle or more, according to the size of the wound's length, then leave space from the head of the wound two fingers' breadth, and stick an needle with a strong thread; and pierce the two skins of the leather with the two pins of the leather inside, until you pierce it from that part, and assemble the two pinheads together four times; then tie a double thread around the needle's half, then assemble the two pinheads of the wound accordingly, and then leave space again, and prick another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and do not cease to do so until the entire wound is closed; and it is suitable that the needles are medium-sized, neither too fine nor too coarse, because the fine needles cut through all the flesh, and the very thick ones cannot enter well enough: therefore they should be medium-sized; and it is not advisable to push the needles too far into the flesh and the leather, lest they do not cut and open the wound before the suturing; and then pierce the pinheads of the needles so that they do not disturb the patient when he sleeps, and put strings or cloths on the pinheads of the needles to tie them tightly, and leave them until the wound is sewn; and this method of suture with the needles is more convenient for small wounds, because there are two needles sewn together in one, and it is that you assemble the two skins of the leather and the two pins together around a needle with a strong thread medium-sized; and when you have pierced all the pinheads completely four times, then pull the needle from the part where you started, in the way of sewing clothes; and put space between each stitch the thickness of a small doily; this costure is suitable for a man who had been stabbed in the abdomen with a knife, and was wounded more than two palms deep, and it involved the intestines well over two palms deep, and the wound was in the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I let the intestines heal first because it had been 22 hours since he was injured, and the wound was closed 15 days after, and I cured him, and he became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the balm had been applied that he would die, but it was a miracle, and I did not apply any medicine because I was in a place where we found no remedies, nor any medicines; and I placed cotton wool on top of the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he became healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and thread from the inside to this point; when it has pierced the skin on the right in the right direction, if you pull out the needle or have threaded the needle again, and pierce it from the other side where it was inside up to that same point; and the understanding of this suturing is such that you sew as the needle-maker sews the hairs, leaving once the plug on one part and covering it with another, until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	In the second manner of sewing, which the Greeks call by its proper name, it is done in this way: whoever does it, brings together the two parts in a natural way and applies one to the other chief with a cloth or syphach close to it, in such a way: prick an needle with the chief of the syphach next to it, and pierce that solely, and let the two joints of the syphach; then turn the needle and make a piercing from the back side until you reach that part inside, from both joints of the syphach; then pierce one and the other from the back side until they reach another two joints on the other side. And this is the most common manner of sewing and is used.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Greeks say that this word means: whoever says so and no one testifies to it, we must sew the belly with two needles, if there is thread in each; and you must push one needle from one side and the other from another, in the way of those who sew corsets; and note that when the rotting is inside the belly, the sewing is more grievous than for others of the bellies.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as those of other wounds: and is that when you find the fresh wound to its entire blood, so that it has moved, you reset the intestine and the cost; then put on powder with vinegar, and if it has moved, put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and cut the thread, and sew the belly, and the bandages; then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, so put on, immediately when they come to move, cotton wool, and shake two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	But you have no need for other medicine in case of simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound may cause communal disease to main joints, it is fitting that you moisten a light linen in hot olive oil or rose oil, and put it inside the arteries, and under the joints; and if he feels pain or rotting in the bowels, which often happens, then bind with clisterize of black wine and vinegar, and likewise if there is rotting coming from the intestine; and you pierce through it, and see that when it is the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is because of the weakness of women, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and its approach to its natural state.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the liver jumps out of the wound, and it is put back in place as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and become dark or black, then it is advisable to cut the person who is black, that bleeding does not come from them, because they have women and arteries; then strike what is between the ligament, and hang the two claws down from the part under the wound until the liver comes out, and the pain is alleviated.
de la routure dou boueil	of the burn from the cauldron
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is swollen, and the wound is small, if it can be restored in some men, because I saw that one man was paralyzed or damaged by a lance in his stomach, and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into an abscess, and from this there came evacuation and vomiting; I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease until he was healed, and the intestine returned.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the sick men had no illness in their stomachs; and it was not so, but he stayed in good health, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, they must tie it in a certain way: take large strips to bind it, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the strips have tied over his mouth, if his lips are strained by the mouth, so that he cannot open his mouth; and then hit the head, and this will hold so that he cannot untie, and then put another strip after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	Cil chief si s'aerdent en l'intestine, and naught troubles the patient, and it may be bound to the intestine with a fine thread cut from an animal's intestine in this manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that is most matted, and then tie to the head of this fine linen thread twisted, then poke the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it back in the rut; and this method of sewing by piercing does not fail but according to the way of hope and chance; and if the wound is large and wide, just as much when it is in one of the intestines' narrow passages, so there is no gain or recovery except through subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula whether it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Things are called a fistula for all wounds or abscesses when they become old, and especially when it is swollen and swollen.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is fitting that I inform you of the treatment for an abscess made by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	We know that abscesses occur in every part of the body; because there are abscesses that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or from the liver, or intestines, or bladder, or on any of the ribs, or on the spine of the back, or at any joint of the hands or feet; and if they occur in a part belonging to the principal member, and resemble its characteristics.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the abscesses of this kind are a source of ill health, and there is only one thing to blame - ignorance; and if there is any abscess that does not come from the place I have described, and you have promised to cure it, and you see it constricting, take a tourniquet made of iron or leather; if the abscess is straight, do so; but if it is crooked, search for one with great subtlety, because the tortuosity of the abscess twists and turns inward; and if the abscess has lost fingers and you cannot find it well by searching with tourniquets, search at the site where the finger was, because the moistures are too short on the surface of a severed finger, and they muddle; then take great care to feel exactly where it is, and ask the patient about the pain he feels in pressing with your hand, and follow his directions to find it; and when you know truly where it is, and whether it is near a joint, or nerve, artery, vein, or any of those things I have described to you, perform according to what I told you, and cut out the corrupt flesh and dead tissue that are within; and then continue with the cure until it is healed; and if the abscess is not healed by these means, if the bones are corrupted by the abscess, take the cauterization as we have said, and if the bone is corroded by the abscess, perform.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	For the veins or nerves that are swollen or inflamed, if as we have said; and if the bones are exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove the bone so that all the corruption is taken out, then treat the wound with salve until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and you go back to your old ways, since before, know that you will not be saved: if expose yourself and ask for treatment as long as you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the limb; and if it is in this state, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not so, know that the corruption has gone too far, that you will not be saved: if there is no other remedy than to rely on nature; and if there are small, corrupted bones, and you can treat them with tongs, if it is a convenient instrument for that purpose, and if there are many bones, then remove all of them; but do not leave one behind; and if moisture makes things worse, and there is no error or fear, tie, moisten, and char, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you cannot remove them after one hour, put a poultice on the wound to check for rotting, and let it sit until the flesh is rotted around the bones, and then they will be lighter; if it's a large bone, like a leg or thigh, just treat the corruption so that the blackness is completely gone from the bone, then heal the wound; but if there is much rotting in the bone, and comes to a knot of bone; you must cover and cover all around the corruption, and then cure until it is smooth.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man in his XXX years, who had a pain in his leg from within the body, so that the materials came to the leg and he ran out of a large abscess, and did not have any other cause for opening; but they cut it open with their foolishness, above where the abscesses opened, and corroded much matter, and became a fistula, and many people thought they had a great disease in their bodies; and most doctors put him on treatment for two years, and there was no cure in the art of hands, until I was called, and came to his leg and saw the medicines with which he was treated, and what corroded by the fistulas gave much sickness to the body; and his skin became red like the juice of a citron.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I have a tent pole in one of these holes, and then I searched for all the holes, and found that some came together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I fell behind, and pierced one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it was corrupt and rotten, and the corruption came all the way to the bone inside; I saw what appeared to be the corrupted bone, and thought there couldn't be any other corruption except for that which I had removed; and I started to treat the wound with medicines on for a long time, and could not suture it; and then I resumed, and discovered the bone just as it was before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and thought of suturing it again; but I couldn't do so until I pierced through one palm-sized piece of the bone, and tore it apart to its full extent, and then restored it with medicines; and he became healthy and sutured quickly, and didn't need to be treated further except for the weakness of the patient, who couldn't bear it, and because of my fear of his death that I had.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood is frequent, but sometimes the patient becomes entirely sane and is born in place of the bone with a hard cartilage, and is of good disposition and has no harm or contrary effect in any way, neither at rest nor at coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, so that it can be done in this manner: take a ligature, and strain the head of the bone which opens, and command that someone stretch it upwards; and put another ligature of linen, thicker than the first one, on top of the cartilage where the bone is removed, and keep the chief, so that you treat the corrupted cartilage downwards, and uncover the cartilage above, as soon as you see it, lest the corrosion touch the cartilage; and put a splint or a table below the bone to cover up the corrupted cartilage; and let it heal for as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and let it heal again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, so uncover the whole flesh; then put in the thorn under, and then sew one side to another the corruption, and make it as long as the corruption is deep, just like we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, so cut the corrupted joint, and sew the bone where it contains of the other part; and if the corruption is on the continuity of two joints, there is no other vein but through the covering; and if the corruption is at the nail of the finger or at the nail of the foot, it is very serious that thing, but you must inquire how the corrosion opens up; and clean it in all kinds of ways that you can, but do not let the vein or the nerve contradict you; and learn that the incisurers and the sewers for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bone and its appearance, and its size and subtlety, and its greatness and smallness, and its hardness.
dou feu	In fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	When the head of the shoulder becomes swollen either because of something inside it or because it is dry; and when you have treated that corruption with medicine and they do not benefit from it, if you wish to cover up that member until the source of the corrosion comes out, so that the patient may escape death by this cause or by the malice, which is more serious, of the limb's fault; and the signs are such that the members become black, so as to seem burned by fire, and afterward the corruption spreads to another part of the body, taking it over from member to member, and infecting all the body; if you hasten to cover up, and this is done through some violent blow from a venomous beast, like a scorpion from the sea and a viper and similar creatures; if there is corrosion in the head of the bones of both sides, then strike, and do not give them any space before coming to hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Et she comes just to the hand, if you strike at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come before the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if you strike at the wrist; and if it passes the wrist, that's death, and there is no use with fire but the quantity of its virtue; and thus do it when the corrosion comes into the bone: if it comes in the first joint, if you strike after the other joint; and if it comes to the bone, if you strike all the bone; and if it mounts to the knee, if you strike at the joint above the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to bind the patient to death; and the manner of striking or soothing the member is such that you tie it above and below, and extend one rope down and another up, and serve the cloth between the two ropes a span wide, until the bone is uncovered; then strike or soothe, and put a cloth from each side a span long, so that the cloth does not touch the healthy part, and comes to the patient with another lesion and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;
