de l’aposteme de l’ungle	From the apostem of the ungula (the claw)
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	The panarice (a painful swelling) is an aposteme that forms under the claw of a finger or toe, or sometimes on other parts; and when it is old and not taken care of, if they come to pick at it, and run and jump so much that they rush to the root of the claw, and by chance they will cut the entire thing; and then comes corruption just at the bone, causing painful pus, and there are swollen fingers, and a foul color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and if the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to copy to it. Iron every remaining flesh that was left behind from the claw, and then cautery the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	In great aid is the cautery if the bones are sound and the joint is healthy; and if the joint presses against the flesh, and begins to prick, and bleeds, then it is advisable to put a splint below the joint so that the bone does not strike the flesh, and push forward and cut with a subtle and gentle blow, and apply medicines hot and corrosive to remove all; afterwards the cure of limbs until he is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosive is in the bone, if you cut it and pull it out, for as long as the bone corrupts, so cannot be healed; and if you see corruption spreading, cut into the flesh just as it was said before, then cure him until he is healed; and if he is iron-hard, and inflamed, and feels great pain, it is advisable to heal him first; afterwards, cut the joint with a sharp knife over, and be careful that the knife does not come too close to the flesh beneath the joint, for the patient will feel too much pain; and if there is, put something above which will soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from a sore ear
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Those who die from blows to the head of some men by chance are all charred, and sometimes they have bones, and at no time do they have an ulcer, and birth does not occur in any of their joints, or birth occurs in a place where none exist.

Those who do not move at all in any part of the body, and those who are born with a jointed limb by chance may also move; the size of that person who is charred is so light, as it seems to be: their size is small in proportion to their root:
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born with the joint's root are crippled to cure: if they hold in the copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When he is born or must be at the rear end, it is advisable to copy the rounded shape just above the bone, then cut the bone to an appropriate size for him, then treat him until he is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The symptoms that occur when the limbs assemble are due to birth, or a sudden injury, or burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient. Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If symptoms appear on either of its two hands with the palm, if it is advisable to treat the wound.
des vils	bad
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	These swellings of the veins are large and swollen with melancholy superfluity, coming to more members of the body; and it happens more often in those who go barefoot and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you give them no purgative of coal, and then heal the wound with the salve of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron remedy is done in two ways: one is to cut them, and treat the black wound; and the other way is to tie the vein, and drain it entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting remedy is done in this way: he raises the leg of a hot water bath very strong, until the large vein becomes subtle; then he strains the leg of the sick person above the gourd up to the area around the knee; then he cuts the vein at one place or two or three times, with a large cut, then lifts and treats the black wound by hand, from head to toe, as long as so much without leaving any, until the virtues of the patient can bear it; and then he ties it, and commands that they eat vegetables free of coal blackness; and repeats the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and harm the sick person.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s'il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et lie arises la jambe d'aigue chaude tant qu'elle deviégne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n'as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If the vein is constricted and twisted and turned together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must break it severely, but do not cover it; and pull it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron rod that you cut the vein with should be curved, and not hollowed out, lest it cuts the vein; for if it were thin, it would cut the vein.
de la voinne civile	of the common woman
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This woman is tied in the legs, in the warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture; but sometimes she is born in other places than in the legs, and this happens because of the corruption that comes from beneath the skin, as it does when a snake enters inside the body and goes down towards the skin, tie between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear to come to the leg with a great inflammation, then change the pus, and start cutting the vein fiercely, as with the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the swelling opens, it is advisable to wrap a piece of linen around one and a half thumbs' length on either side of the knee, and the vein, and leave the linen on the leg, and at all times when the swelling is near, wrap the linen around the vein and the new flesh; and if it's too long, cut off a part and wrap up the remainder, and do not cover its root, until it has all come out; because if you cut it, it will return into the wound, and bring abscesses and putrefaction with it, and bad disease; therefore it is necessary to treat this vein slowly, one inch from the head, and do not leave anything behind in the body; and it happens sometimes that when this vein is treated for two palms or X, it issues out of X inches long, and when you cut it, it flows into I parts or punctures, and drains to the bottom, so that all the matter inside is empty, and the patient is made to drink medicine on one day every four days, then the cure goes as for abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes to this vein a great flow of blood comes, and the same thing when she opens in the joint of the foot, or on the foot, and it comes out much from cuts, and where there is bleeding; treat then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between leather and armor
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "disease of the ox" in our land because it often affects cows, and it has many worms that are born between leather and armor, which move and flow throughout the body, and cause pain in every limb, until they burst through the leather or where they are going, and jump out; and are infested with some putrefaction of humors, as serpents, lumps, and ascarides, or belly; and one doubts its malevolence, because when it moves through the body, and rises to the head, and often reaches the eye, by chance entering, and destroying the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture. de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vackirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and moves from one limb to another; and I have seen this myself what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I went to see a woman who was ill, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of one of her arms; and I looked at it afterwards, as if it were a worm on my shoulder, just as quickly as anything else, like living silver when it cuts into her flesh again; the pain left that limb and attached itself to the shoulder, and then a little after it ran through all the body, so that she went back in the other arm; then she told me that she was going into convulsions, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I'm sorry I can't help with that.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	I'm sorry I can't help with that.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see treating this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens so as we have said, then take a sharp knife and hasten to cut from above and below at the same time, and cauterize the wound; and if you do not see with your eyes, then let the doctor who is skilled in cutting veins, use foul-smelling pills, such as serpent's pills, and similar ones.
des saiettes	the arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse according to their appearance and according to the place where they pierce the body or where they enter.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows is that there are those with great points and small ones, spines, and sewing needles; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and the one that pierces into any member, it pierces according to two manners: in the principal members such as brain, liver, gallbladder, spleen, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it then pierces into any of these members and the signs of death appear as I will tell you later, if this happens to you: it is necessary that you remove the extraction of this arrow, because the death comes after in many situations; and when this sign does not appear to you, and the arrow has pierced deeply, then take away, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seat when it bleeds or breaks out is that it is near the left nipple and feels as if it were pierced in a hard thing, not empty; and by chance the seat moves as much as the fingers do, and in black bile it comes, cold and sweaty, and fainting: this we know to be doubtful that death has come.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that has not been swollen is only without any swelling of pus jumping out from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, they gasp high and feel cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow bleeds into the covering of the breast, it is near the small ribs; and a great amount flows out with great pain, and they gasp; and all the limbs of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If they let the arrow shot into the belly fall or it passes through the stomach by chance, so that some of the undigested meat is left behind from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the arrow shot into the belly or stomach passes through the intestine without coming to a stop by any grain of wool on its surface, and there is no hope for recovery from the wound or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the arrow shot into the bladder and its contents pass out through a passage and come out with great urination, and the patient feels extreme pain, it is clear that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, arm, back, spine, fists, chest, and legs, and all the limbs appearing to be sound according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it's not venomous, as I told you, so that you should do the same thing.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to me at home with an arrow stuck in the throat or neck at the root of the nose: I tried to cut it out, and pulled it out from another side under the fatty tissue of the ear, and it was quickly healed.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And on another occasion I pulled out an arrow that had lodged in the fatty tissue of the cheek under the skin below, and the arrow was extracted, and it could only reach as far as the point into a wooden bow, and the arrow was quite long, like one made from a Turkish arrow, all light, to the ears; the operation was successful, and I did not meet with any other bad consequences.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And tie a tourniquet around the neck of a Christian, and use an Arab tourniquet on the ears: I sheared the beards, and carefully tied them until I had finished, and the Christian became well.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I tied a tourniquet to the one who was lying on his stomach, and he thought he was dying; but after 30 days had passed, he did not improve in any way; I cut under the tourniquet, and put it back in place, and it worked, and there were no bad accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And I visited another home who had a tourniquet cut on his back or buttocks, and the wound was sealed; and the tourniquet remained inside him for a while, and he did not change his natural disposition, nor found any discomfort in any of its works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man, to whom a quiver arrow pierced his face, and caused wounds; and he suffered thus for a long time in great pain; and many of his fellow patients had similar symptoms.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And he shot an arrow at the king's servant who was struck by it in the neck, and was slightly leaning to the right side; for three days he had been suffering from this.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched for it everywhere with great subtlety, and could not find it; but he felt a pinching and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it might be the point of the arrow, so I applied a poultice to his liver and stomach area, because he had swelling there; and an arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I let the boils on my hands dry out and resolved the wound above, and kept the patient for such a long time, until he felt the arrow the day before yesterday inside his nose; and he says to me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put medicine with corrosive properties on the wound by hand for days, until it was dry, and I tried it, and you felt the head of the arrow which dried up in your nose; then I adjusted the opening of the wound by that medicine, so that the head of the arrow appeared clearly visible; and I pierced well into the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine for three months, and then I cut off the bandage, and from one side and the other, and it wouldn't come out; therefore I didn't cease to try and invent ways using tools until I got a pair of tongs made one day, according to how its shape would come in at the end of this chapter, as we have tried, until we took it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they judge that the cartilaginous piece of the nose cannot be restored; I will restore it then, and the wound was closed, and the patient became completely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of extracting arrows, so that you apply your cure to what I do not tell you, because books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters understand a little bit more than many things, and deal with what is present and failing, new work and new instrument, at the removal of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not issue from the members where they are stuck unless by two kinds: either through the vein itself or through another part; and whichever side sticks faster into the vein, now it is entering the veins, and never again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	Instruct the patient to let them wait now until the wound is covered and clean; and so if they stick it into the bone and cannot come out, leave it thus for some days and move it every day; and then it will heal, and if it does not heal, if you pierce into it thoroughly at all times, till the bones are enlarged, and then take it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if an arrow is stuck into the bone of the neck, and stays just above one of the bones in the skull, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned to the patient: do not treat it, but let it stay until it becomes even after some days, for if the arrow comes just above the brain, it will kill.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come just above the brain, and the patient remains sick for some days without a worse accident, it will work out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she is very swollen in this way and cannot get out of the wound, then I administer tartar emollient around it, as I have told you; then treat the animal until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in the animal's body so that we cannot see it, and if you can't get a good look at it, then if you feel for it, if it has any fitting instruments, and if you can't get into the wound because of its tightness and the depth of the arrowhead, and there are no bone or nerve tissue around it, then try to pull out the arrow as long as the wound is large; and if you can pull it out, and it has something in the arrow that keeps it there, such as a piece of wood half-way through the joint, then extract the part you can, and break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull them out, until you get it to come out; and be careful not to break the arrow, so that you can pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, if the wound is made up to the level of the joints until it is painful, then remove it, because the extraction hurts.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the blood of the vein is made to counteract this, so that you do as we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and guard against the incision on the nerve and the vein, and put in meat so that you may move to treat the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form which he was in when the arrow hit him, for this is the greatest aid that can be done, and if you cannot do it, so that they put him according to what signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from the other side, or where there is an opening in it, or if the skin is inflamed straight in so that you can see or feel it: then take hold of it, making a cut above it, until the tongs can get hold of it, and then pull it out; but now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if she is held in the bone, then turn your hand around it, so that she enters into the bone, and enlarges the bone, then pull.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if she cannot come out, then leave it some more, and then continue the extraction until she comes forth; and if it is stuck in the arrow shaft, pour the entire contents of the arrow shaft into it; and if it sticks, then administer powder, so that you apply an instrument with hair on it, where the point of the arrow shaft enters into the hair of the instrument; and then pour, and if the arrow shaft has come up, pour again into it, to help with the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow shaft is touched, so that you can, then it is best to copy all the flesh around where the venom is, and then treat the wound as it needs.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to cover the wound if it comes out through the skin or flesh or into the vent or at the costey and it is close; and you can cover up, if it has come out; and guard the vein and the nerve, and then pull it out, and then sew the wound, if it is proper; and keep treating the patient until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to that of a bird's beak, and thus it is:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the forceps with the hook-like claw is similar to that of an bird's feather, to push against the tip of the arrow.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the tongs for holding and grasping is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins on the body common.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Veins that heal are XXXI in number, because there is one head XVI, which is to say: two branches behind the ears, called "herbech", and two arteries in each temple; and two veins on either side of the eyes, called "aspire"; and a vein at the forehead; and a vein at the top of the nose; and two ligatures on the neck; and two veins above the lips, which are called "augeherich"; and two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that heal commonly are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is located on the left side of the chest, and they call it "vein of the head"; the medial is called "fast", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and they call it "vein of the heart"; the basilic is on the right side of the chest, and they call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the diaphragm, and that is the one that heals, which opens up clearly under the pocket.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The patient's arteries are located between the auriculate and anular bones, and there are two veins; in the leg and foot, there are three veins: one is below the galleon with a sac at the left shoulder-side, and the second vein is at the ankle on the right side; and there is a vein called "nese", which is located in the other ankle; and in the other leg, there are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The veins located behind the ears aid with purging of ancient bowel movements and with emigration; and the qualities of those who have experienced this are as I tell you, and is that you raise the head of the sick person, and rub the neck or the veins with a rough cloth; then pull the patient's chin up so that the two veins appear behind the ears on both sides in two levels: when you see these, if they touch your foot, and you feel the pulse beneath it, then sign off; then take the lancet, and squeeze through below the vein until you reach the bone; then lift your hand to the entire vein, and cut and the skin and the vein well twice must do so that they are traversed; and make the incision and cautery first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Instruct the patient that when two arteries are cut in the temples, it is an old and severe pain, and a sight accustomed to the eyes, and in the chest of tears; and the qualities of the sufferer are such as I say: and it is that the patient strangles his neck until the two veins open widely; and feels the hairs below their tendon, and then signs; then lifts the scar above the vein towards his neck index finger, and pushes the lancet down, and lifts the vein up, and strikes, just as you have done in two other veins, and do the wound according to your need; then release the patient, and place your index finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then form a stitch, and leave it until it is healed; and we have talked about their cutting and extraction, and how to begin this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sickness of the vein on the front is worth as much as the sickness of the head due to ancient face maladies, and emigraine, and redness; and the qualities are such that patients twist their neck until they appear; then take up the instrument called "fosseur", which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And set the point on the vein, and stand above with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; then lift the patient's neck, and tie the vein so that it is healthy and never have a great redness.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	But it is not good that the cuts are too sharp; and the wound crooked, because the bone is near, and by chance, breaks the cut when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The patient of the two veins that are in the left shoulder should aid his eyes, and to the vein, and to the redness, and to the swelling, and to the infection in the eye; and the qualities of their disease are such that the patient strains his neck by twisting from any bond, as before; then heal it, and let the healing pass through a small piece of wood, one piece long, one piece wide, for there is no leather.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the swelling is subtle, in case it breaks; then sew up the wound, as much as you need to, and then tie it with a cloth, and tie well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The swelling of the vein in the neck is very serious, and causes a fever, and soreness, and diseases of the eye, so that it migrates and redness comes into the eye, and especially when it is old; and the qualities of the disease are such that the patient strains his neck, then twists his neck to your left hand, and takes out the thin piece of wood, and puts it inside the gap between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well, and now he will start to heal; and do not go too fast in front, and sew up the wound according to your need, then tie a night, for it is very quickly restored; and this is the shape of the thin wood:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to tie the two wounds tightly, and at the beginning of treatment, and due to many illnesses, and emphysematous fever, and corrosions, and herpes, and estiomenes; and their qualities of the wound are such that patients remove their collarbone on one side and the other, just as we have said; and let the masters stand above the patient's head, and patients sit in a separate seat, then cut a vein on the long finger slightly wide, then draw the blood temperately, or until it is necessary; then do another cut on the other vein, then release the bandage, and bind the veins moderately, that the patients do not choke; and let him just leave at night, so that the wound be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	About the wounds of the feet.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The patient's blood from his lips should be applied to the nose, and to prevent corruption of gums, and split lips, and to apply ointment.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the blood should be done by sitting the patient in front of you, and constricting his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at both veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which can be recognized by their black color and because they have small, black marks: strike one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, strike the larger of each part, and do it for both the above and below veins, as it is a same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the blood from under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The sick of the veins that are below the tongue help after the head is cut, and it's at the constricting of the throat, and with eye diseases, and mouth diseases; and the qualities in healing so that the patients get between your hands in front of the sun, and lift the tongue, and look under each cost (side), a black vein: heal then both and do not go too far into it, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the hand that are commonly cut are cut according to two manners: either by poking into the whole flame of myrtle tree, or by olive oil subtle like the cuts make it, and called "anesil"; and they are large and subtle according to the largeness and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame mint is very famous and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the clean veins of large, deep wounds with great blood flowing out, and which contain big blood clots and troubles; and this is the form of the flame olive oil.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtle in point, and is for healing the small veins subtle, or where there are subtle blood clots.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic salve, which is one of these veins, helps to cure all the diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen; and it is fitting for the master that he cures with it, and that he warms himself from the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and blood comes out when we start bleeding, then it should be stitched, just as I said; and he shouldn't be pinched too hard, but cut like an animal.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the gallbladder does not open clearly, then it should be removed, and another taken in its place; or if you want to drain blood from it, or to sew it up on the side of the arm: it opens clearly; and cut into the flesh like an animal, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you see a swelling in the arm of the wounded man, then so too should you remove the arm; touch the swellings until you know how many are there; then mark them with chalk, and bind up the arm, and cut into the vein like an animal; and be careful not to pierce the artery when you see the swelling, for it is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it coming out in the upper part like the urine of a child and they are red and subtle, know that it's without an artery: hurry then, and put your thumb long on them, then take off your thumb if they don't sting, for this happens many times; tie up the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the sick person; and be cautious, and do not move it until they are cured.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If they do not get a sting from it, and it comes out, and the medicine is not present in them, then strike the artery if it opens up, for the head of the vein will be returned; stung are they.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a scab of fistula, and make an incision in it, and take one of the halves and tie well to the other day; if they do not get stung, it is good; if this is not so, then heal as we have said, with the powders that sting the blood; for the stinging does not weigh more on those dispositions than on small wounds of the flesh, and the power of the tied arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	Instruct the patient to apply a poultice of wine in the middle so that he treats wounds on the top of the head and below the body, since it is composed of basilic and cephalic blood, as we have said; and it is fitting for the lord that he takes care of the nerve that is below, and if he presses too hard and cuts into it, and the nerve becomes inflamed, and the wounds are painful, and by chance it cannot be healed; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in anyone due to its subtlety, it is fitting that you cleanse the wound with a lancet first; and carefully take away the nerve to his own power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The application of the cephalic blood is assisted, where he treats wounds on the head and assists with the eyes; and it is fitting to heal by applying a poultice of olive oil or myrtle oil, because this is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	All things considered, it is best to seek the lighter treatment first, and do not grieve anything if one has to try it for the first time, and start again; and by chance, some swellings may occur in a few people, on the first try, but they will not harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about healing is that healing is not possible only to preserve health and to remove impending diseases; and if the wound is made in one of the three veins: head (cerebral), fast (lower), or basilic (groin); it must be done at the beginning of prayer, in autumn and winter after fasting, when the sign of replenishment appears; and it should be done on the first day or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The sick person who is attended has no fixed remedy for diseases, but rather when they need it in the morning or at night, in all hours and for all time; and it's not suitable to heal children until they are 12 years old, and pregnant women except during the first six months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And it's not suitable to heal an elderly person who has passed their 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some people wish to be healed in any way, if they must fast the intestines of a light purgative, if they have much retained faeces, so that the veins do not constrict the superfluous parts of the intestines and cause harm to the principal members; nor does he heal himself who is too salty from meat, or who has fever, until it is so bad, or dropsy; and if a person is sick after colic and vomiting, and deceleration of the belly, and frequent urination, and travel, watching, and lying down, and that which kills the virtue, either by some kind of weapon or through the body; then sublimate the humors, do not make them too thick, with food and drink and medicines, if it has any power; then take a bath, if no other remedy is available, to sublimate the sickness, and become healthy from the side of the inflamed skin to the third, as we have said; and beware that day of work, pain, luxury, and similar things; and be bound and free, and let the sages be more high than those who are healed, and rub his arms two or three times, then strain the bandage in the middle, because when it is too tight or loose, he cannot correct it without; and then rub him with his own hands, until the veins swell and feel on; then apply a poultice of hot fat oil, put some salt from his left hand under that vein where he wants to heal, so that the vein does not fail and fail to be injured.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For in the veins that are like strings to the healer, and for those that are so full of windiness, when you put the flame on them, they pull back into flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if he opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, because of this it is advised that the healers be aware of such things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it is good; but if not, then again you resume it a little below where it was or above hastily, if the swelling has gone.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is there and the patient fears it, let him leave one day or two, and do not bind his arm: by chance he will come to an abscess on his foot; or do not enter the bath, then resume the treatment as he pleases. And if the wound is small, or if you carefully apply subtle pressure, and you doubt that it will not burst so much as you see, be firm in that same wound with all the flame directly; and open it a little hastily, so that the swelling may be there; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the swollen limb, do not start the dressing again, and put a little bit of lard oil on it, because it alleviates the body from pain, and is moistened by the oil; and thus administer the oil in each wound that you heal the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and this same thing also applies to an arrow when one puts it on the limb; so subtlety and prudence when it's too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which happens often, especially when there are no openings in the vein only at those times or after the vein is cut open, then quickly apply, and put the limb on an moistened sponge soaked in water and with some flour, and hold it for one hour; it is to be done after the opening of the vein, and if it stays on the limb for some days without any more pain or swelling, it will not harm. If you see, place some aloes or mirror made from gum camphor, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times occurs an abscess and appearance at the skin of the basilica: put then your hand on it, and if you find the bone soft with pressure of the hand, that is the evil appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then that you do not put anything of what we have said, because by chance you cut into an artery; but make it bleed dry for hardening the bone, then treat with another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each one according to the quantity of their virtue and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if the wound is black, let it breathe until it becomes red; and if you see a large one, let it breathe until it becomes subtle; and if it's too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, and it is fitting for him who is weak and strong; and if he needs extraction of blood, make the wound larger and wider; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is more likely to heal sooner and oftener, and it must be healed in cutting across, not with force; and this way of healing is safe from the corruption of blood and the crippling of nerves, and is better than healing short or long.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him whose blood needs to be cut open, it is fitting to give a moist pain in juice of pomegranate; if he is scorched, apply the wound three times or four with blood; and if his complexion is cold, apply a moist pain in syrup of honey, or in syrup of mulled wine with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, until it has a good odor.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if the hand is drawn back, after a great quantity of blood has flowed out, it is necessary to drink broth of vinegar and odorant sweet syrup, and use other things that we have spoken of in this division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if it wants to extend a certain limb and make its wound better again, when he is weak due to great blood loss, it is necessary, as much as possible, according to the quantity of his continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to extend some limb after the first bleeding, and his strength is great, then it will heal in 7 hours after the first bleeding, or on the next hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wishes to be healed from another part, should he need to be healed on the second day or on the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflamed, then let it alone and do not bind it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the wound needs to be treated a second time, let it be cleaned in either the same vein as before, or in another vein, or on the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that is cut in the arm is healed because of the blood of the head, since it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of healing if it is that the patient puts his hand in hot water, until the flesh is red; then tie it moderately, so that the vein appears well; now treat the wound with the cross, not too long or too wide; and if they are large punctures, heal them well near the joint of the hand, and if they do not come out, put the hand in hot water again, and let the wound drain into the water, until you have enough; and if this is done, do not put the hand back in hot water, for it sets more in winter than in summer; and the healing of this vein is saved from all others, without artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The sickle of the salvation of the right hand is worth for all kinds of illnesses of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand, and pour into hot water, until the vein is cleared; if it is seen; and if it's cut across, and you copy it throughout, do not grieve anything; and don't go too far, because the nerves are raw from all being squeezed out of place, and then put the hand back in hot water, unless they are frozen in the wound, and can't come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have cut into the vein as needed, so that it's sealed quickly with oil and thread for a quick repair, and do the same for each part.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sickle of the salvation in the left hand is worth for mouse illness, and do as I told you over to the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the spine is worth its weight in all diseases that are inside the body, such as those of the marrow, and retention of phlegm, and disease of the bones, and joints, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of his sickness is such that when the sick person drinks a mixture of earth and hot water, and rubs on the vein until it bursts, and binds above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot they go out much pain, then cure is possible if you make it either larger or wider, or at the ankle.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cure it on the foot, take heed of the swine that are below, and cut away the sickness as in cutting out a tumor; and let the fester.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If they cannot come out, then put the foot into water, and let it well drain the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	If it is necessary to cut first time, then resume the second on top a little bit, for the flesh is salt; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do it evenly with the other foot.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic vein is at the heel, and its pain is similar to that of the groin when it's cut.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of its cut are such that if the patient drinks from it, and you strain above the heel for four times while twisting, because otherwise the vein does not open; and when it opens, then cut in all directions as you can, and across it; and be careful not to copy the flesh, for the flesh is thin, and it is very returned at home hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find it, so the healthy blood will be released from the open vein and the back of the foot to the small toe, and ward off the evil spirits; and make as much pressure on the wound that you see, and then remove the bandage, and put cotton and bind with a cloth; now she is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of wind sickness
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Wounds are made from horns, or nails, or nails; and wind sickness is done in two ways: either by striking and attracting the wound, or by striking.
