Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this wind sickness which is done by striking is in two ways: either it is all fire, or not. Wind sickness made by striking and draining the wound is done in thirteen places of the body; for one is at the summit of the head; and others are on the neck; and there are two more on the left and right sides of the neck; and there is a windiness under the chin; and there are windings between the shoulders; and there are windings above the knees; and there are windings in both arms; and there are windings in both legs; and there are windings on the two ankles; and this sickness does not touch the wound, except for some small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and by doing so it weakens no one, just as one does when draining a vein; and it is not suitable to be administered, nor all fire or smoke, in any disease that comes from overeating, until all the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	When we see these signs, and especially when it is coming to its third month, we instruct the patient to have an operation after three hours on the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sickness of the spleen helps to reduce swelling of the head … that comes to the eyes, and it is not suitable for this to happen after the evacuation of all the body; and this operation is in place of the splenic pain, and it is not suitable for anyone who has a hot constitution, or who has catarrh, because this causes much harm; and therefore it is not suitable for those who keep vigil, or who have cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become blind, and therefore they need to put the vacuum one piece further down by the diagnosis of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wound on the neck is in place of the vein of the head and basilica, and because of this it causes her to tighten up with pain, splitting the canal of the belly, and burning, and repletion; and they should not push, for if she tightens too tightly, then an obstruction or stomach turn, or a gut ache occurs.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The windings are on both sides of the neck if it causes pains in the head, eyelids, and migraines, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and is similar to the vein of the basilica; therefore you should command the master that he presses his hand while putting it in, so as not to cut the artery, and do not hesitate for a moment.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The windings under the chin cause mouth disease, and gum corrosion, and similar illnesses in the mouth; and are like the veins of both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders is equal to a sickness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings of the sides are equal to having three large veins in the arm, because they cause blood loss from these great veins; and instruct the lord that he should not bleed too much, for the arm is bare of flesh, and knows beneath its skin and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The windings above the haunch are equal to hemorrhoids from the fundament, and other diseases, and it is necessary that they be large, and of hair, so as to treat them well; and by chance, if they are subtle, they will break; and thus make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The windings of the legs heal quickly, because they attract blood from all the body, and are equal to old pains from rains, and of the mares, and of the bladder, and cause swelling; and are in place of two sores, and two knees, and everywhere else, for they weaken the body after a long time, and bring death in more frequent conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	Instruct the patient to put on the ventouse first when it is empty and successful, then hold it steadfastly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing so until you see the limb turn red and swollen, and appear the redness of the wound; then close again, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have such a severe pain, and beware: if one must strike once only, and it is advisable to make large wounds and deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is not large, you should strike twice: once to subtend the path of the big wound.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the wound is very thick, it is advisable to strike a third time; and when we want to apply a little of the wound's juice little by little, we should only strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	Instruct the patient to let blood flow much if they wish; and if it does not come forth quickly, then frequently bleed them again. And if their skin is thick, prick firmly at the end, until the blood flow appears suddenly, and oil of vinegar dissolves easily: if this works, use oil of violet, or oil from almonds sweet, or oil of cucumber seed; and if you prefer to use wine, then use oil of cresson, or of herbs, or chamomile, or similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if they flow out thick and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or balsamite, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if those with healthy skin have large pores, do not put oil on them, but rather wash after the application of rose water, or cold water, or elderberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain berry water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And they who have much moisture in them, will rise up from this place, or from the dew of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large surflowing, will rise up from old wine, or from the dew of rue, or from the decoction of anise or camomile, or similar things; and do not think they can recover by suction before the bath, nor in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two hours; and do not sleep afterwards, because they must be suctioned and because it is being suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And it is advisable for those who recover are choleric and have too much heat and inflammation; if they take cold things, such as apples, grapes, endives, and lettuce at the same time, and similar things; and eat small portions, and chicken broth, and roasted shoulder meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles qui sont mises sur le foie, et sur la mice, et podagre, et sur le ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie de ferir ou lez, et ne le fait on fuer que pour atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscosite qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sur le ventre et sur la boude pour amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l'opilation, ou desaert la piere de son lez; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sur le foie et sur la mice quant il i a ventosite retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides pour sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d'aigue tede, si com en maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c'on emplisse la ventouse d'aigue chaude sole, ou d'aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the ventouse administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two fingers of length and half a palm from the bottom, and one finger’s breadth on either side of the middle, as if to put an arrow, and so soft that it will not hurt the patient when placing it on the member; and in the middle have a cross bar of iron or steel, to tie a cord around, and they are large and small, according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the ventouses of children are different from those of adults, and thin ones are not good for fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus you must put this ventouse on the member: take the cord of wax or linen and tie it around the middle bar that is in the ventouse, so that the light may be at the bottom of the ventouse and not burn the patient; then place it on the member, and let the two fingers be above the little notch that we have said, so that when you want to release it, if there is vapor, then remove the ventouse; and take up the linen as before, and reapply it frequently, if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of those with pleurisy in the lungs, who are ailing with fever, have no pulse or pulse is weak, and are not nourished except when they are full of fever, and are placed only on the limb, and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Those without pulse are nourished only in limbs where you cannot put a ventouse due to smallness, like lips and gums, and similar ones; and when they have nasal discharge, like phlegm or pus, and other similar things; and the qualities of the user if is that as soon as you find those without pulse which are in clean running water without risk of hurt, take them; and put one into clean running water, until they become familiar with it, and have nothing in their stomachs; and then let them drink from vein and ventouse, and then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the ulcers; and when they are full, and start to flow, if that can be done, put a ventouse on them, because this is very good.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If it is not so, lift the limb in a safe place, and then into water, very well, and then expect; and if they are healthy too soon after their wounds, cover them with a wet cloth of linen in cold water, and put on, until they are stopped; and if they multiply, cover them with vitriol broken, or gales, and similar things, until it is stopped; or you put over the limb two-thirds of raw peels, and leave them so that they dry to the limb, so will now be cured; and if you have more need, take other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not heal on their own, rub the limb with fresh pus, or you pierce them with a needle until they bleed, and then put them on, and as soon as you feel that they are bleeding, they will dry; and when you see that they are stopping, cover with powder of alum and salt broken, or cinder, so they will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	The Book of Injuries begins
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is used for restoring breaks and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the art of cutting is rarely found in old books or letters, and no one has read them; and because of this, our science is lost in our land, for I have not found any good book; and I know nothing, except by the science of old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated it well, through experiment, and by my experience in life; and I have explained here what is contained, and have condensed it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we declare in the prologue of this book the sums of speech and the chapters where the wise men set their understanding, and dwell on the truth, so that those who are proven to have learned it can learn this noble art, and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When any break or dislocation or twisting or crushing occurs on the body, it is necessary to hasten to heal the sick person from one side and the other, if nothing else hinders you, in order to be weak as flesh, sickness, or old age; or if the joints are not very swollen or too cold; and when he takes hot food, that is to say, cold drinks, and charred chicken and venison, and does not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and does not overindulge in flesh which fills the veins with blood, until you have a clear sign of an abscess or expansion of matter in the limb; if the patients return to their previous government before they get worse.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore themselves, it is fitting that one should nourish the patient with foods that make a large amount of growth, or where there is viscosity, just as bread cooked in water, and meat, and eggs, and fat, and veal, and fish, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For nourishment to have effect it is presented by muscles and grows faster than the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the old and decayed bones cannot be well restored or soldered according to their nature because of dryness of the limbs, or those who are too tender, like the bones of small children; but there is no cure: remove from the broken bone a large tendon that attaches itself to the limb together, so that it is joined as before; and do not leave entirely its work, and for this reason they should nourish with gross foods, just as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or the arm, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that occur at the joint, and others when cutting, just as the length of a pin to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with an open wound, and a fracture with just a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each type has its own instrument and proper tool in the restoration, according to what comes from memory; and it is known that fractures of the bone are recognized by the twist of the limb, and they open well when neglected, and sound with pressure on the finger; and if there is no twist or knot on the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, unless there is a fracture; but he can still have a twist, a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not convenient to move your hand, but apply medicines that come after this, and then restrain it now with subtlety.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that if a fracture is in the arm, and the two parts are disjointed, you must now put them together equally, so that they heal; and if they begin to heal quickly, let one day pass, until the fracture is closed; then set it at ease as lightly and easily as possible, and know that the restoration of this part is lighter than the restoration of that, where there are pieces.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it's two parts that have been extended, whether it's a main limb or a small member, or both cords, or one cord and a small member; then set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the limb that were broken are reduced, remove by all means the additional pieces in their place at the joints as much as you can, and beware that through your work there will not come to the patient an injury or pain; and add well both the two heads of the bones according to the better forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if he feels well in the hand as it seems to you that it is not good: if the dress is done beautifully, and not too tightly restrained, nor pressed so as those do who make come by their work with a hot and painful contraction on the member, as we have had many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at a point, if you carefully keep the patient from moving, neither watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner, and well guard that the limb be so secure it does not feel a single pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not at a point, and you should therefore place him in such a position that he does not feel any pain; and you must carefully keep that he be placed correctly, so that twisted movements do not occur when restored, and the qualities of the broken member are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	A body part is broken in many different sizes and shapes and forms.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	There are small members, such as fingers and toes: if they are small, you should wrap soft cloth around them; and for larger ones, like thigh and calf: it is necessary to wrap with a wider and thicker rope. Because large ropes encircle the entire big member, and tighten all parts evenly, so that there is no hole; then tie in gentle loops, three or four according to the member, and hold your hand tight on the whole rope, then go to the top of the break and tighten less, until the break gets loose a little, the thread softens bit by bit, until you grasp a big part of its healthy flesh. Then take another rope, and turn back over to the injured side; then tighten moderately, not too hard nor too soft, as we have said in the first part above; then put cloth strips or draperies between the ropes, until they are all even, then tie everything from top with a bandage, and then put your stitches well made on it, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if it has an inflammation or abscess, apply soothing ointment to the abscess and let him be in that state for some days; then stretch out his joints, and tie them with a cane of one-fifth width, or of a log used for mallets, or palm tree fragments, and do so according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the bandage which you put on the break be one finger wider and longer than the others; and so as long as is needed for the limb of small or large size; then tie up the joints just as you did in the first place, and above the break with a thread like this before, if it were so tight that it could not be loosened, and is more tightly wound, it will be less so; and it is necessary that the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, but of good quality linen, because if the thread is too thick, as I tried to do with my works among the foolish ones who make their bandages from twisted linen ropes, and this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too subtle, and does not suit at all that there should be between each joint less than two fingers' width.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is sick from the chisel of a spear after being struck in his healthy joints, then he must tie over those wounds with linen cloth, or woolen rag, so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bones are broken, I will tell you the cure as follows.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to strain the bones of all the limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Because when the members are large, it is not necessary to put in bones on the first day, only after five days or seven days, or longer, according to the safety of the abscess that will follow; and here is the manner of the ancient physicians for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: you take flour from near the walls of the mill, mix it with a great amount of egg, and make this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of applying plaster to restore fractures in various conditions, especially women and small children, because it's neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of applying plaster to restore breaks and dislocations and twists: take beeswax and lanolin and olive oil and asafetida and gum arabic and myrrh and aloes, ana V; alechil VIIII; and make a powder, and mix with honey with a little vinegar; if the complexion of the skin is hot, use this plaster, for it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and saves many lives.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of applying plaster that is good for twists: take myrrh and bismuth, ana V; mirre and aloes, ana VIIII; caice VI; bolic armenic X; grind well, and confit with water or a little vinegar, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to treat joint pain and swelling from the joints and bones, take their limbs, and ease the following pain, and use the bone, and break the fracture: take a new linen, and apply the poultice in easy and in oil cooked, and place on the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These poultices do not restore health, but they are good for soothing abscesses and proper bones, the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to treat broken bones that restore the bone: take dried leaves of fig and leaves of earthy parsley, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to treat broken bones for restoring the bone and for making the remaining part of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take roots of wormwood, camomile, violet flowers, wheat flour from fenugreek, one part each; and grind, and mix with wine, and warm the limbs by mixing it with vinegar of coriander moist or pure vinegar, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of treating an abscess more forcefully than the first when pus comes to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of wormwood, and the seed of flax, balsamum, melilot, and sanssouci, and violet flowers and camomile from all one part; and grind, and mix with vinegar of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Iporcras is said in his book to not put on a broken limb for restoration unless he does a salve made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and says it should be neither too moist nor too dry.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that we must put a linen cloth on the broken limb, to restore, putting dry things in moist ones, as we have said and practiced.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of binding that is worth a broken limb and pain: take mullets and hog's trotters, or quails' feathers, and silk equally, and break them up, and make it bind the limb.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove it a little later, and take care that the sick person does not feel any pain, or that their bones are out of place; if not, do not remove by force. But if pain comes to the limb, or pruritus, with rest or swelling, hasten, and remove it, and release the binding now; and take a light cloth, and a wet sponge from the sea, and plunge into water, and lift up the limb, until the pruritus stops, and the pain is assuaged. Then let it rest for an hour, then put on a dry linen cloth, moistened in water or olive oil rose, and tie around a nut, until you are sure of no abscess; and calm down the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume gentle binding, and do not strain it too hard as before; and be subtle until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is swollen and red and painful and inflamed, I have taken out the bone in its entirety, and you must apply plaster and bind it again, if it recurs, as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not happen to the limb what we have said, do not release it more than after three days or four or five or seven; and never let it stay for twenty days, as long as the fracture heals, and approaches the bone again; then hold the constraint tighter than before, and fatten up the flesh, as I told you before. And if you see the limb drying out more than is necessary, know that nothing good will come of it; therefore, give rise to the swelling with hot water tea, every time you release it, and this should be done on a third day, and add a little later; by this operation, then cut off the swelling from the member, and treat harshly what the foolish doctor does, which is to ruin the limb: that's bad, and if there are any painful operations, I see nothing but straining and overstretching it.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of fractures and various shapes, and the causes are predetermined; for there are fractures that are caused by the impact of a sword, and they pierce through the bone just beneath it, like a blow or a punch; and for this reason is called this kind of fracture "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword strikes the bone from above and pierces it completely, this is called an "absolute" fracture; and there are injuries resulting from both large and small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has piercing, or cutting, or fracture of bone, or strike on the stone, or on the chair beneath the stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if he has a persistent fracture, which is near the thread that is under the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is big or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is covered in the bone with a skin as fine as ours, and the fracture is small, and because of this it is called "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is made by striking an object with stone, or falling, or some similar thing, and it pushes the piece of bone inside, and the little hairs are as they do when the cauterist heats up the cauldron over the cauldrons; then the pieces go in.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens to those who have moist bones in their head, like the head of a child; and it occurs in all these kinds of fractures where small pieces are separated, just like stones. And I will speak on his behalf.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by pulling apart at them, and investigating with the knife, and the corrupted flesh which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of hair is known by this: when the bone is discovered and rubbed above, it opens up the dark fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be careful for adverse accidents in the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, paleness, fever, eyes that are swollen and red, and other similar signs, then he cannot recover without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an extraordinary accident and you hope for recovery, as you begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the pain comes first to you, and it's in winter, so you should remove the bone in front of the fortieth day on a full moon when you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	But if it's in this state, so that you hasten to remove the bone in front of the fifteenth day, instead, the wound under the bone will become infected, and accidents like those we have described will occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone break comes just to the covering of the brain, so that you should cut into the part that is broken thus: and be sure to take hold of the patient's head, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and as near the shape of the wound as you can, since there will be bleeding when you uncover the bone or abscess, assist with what is needed, and it is that you fill the cavity with moist drapes soaked in olive oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses are calmed down, and be sure of no further bleeding; then begin to remove the bone, and this is done in two ways of operation:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then let him drink another portion larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a variety of cuts, some are three points and others wider, and they should be sharp and made of iron; and work lightly, lest you strike the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, it is advantageous that you pierce through it entirely, so that you administer cuts with saws, not piercing only into the skin, but leaving space over the point of an inch or a circle, lest the point pass beyond the bone; and it's advisable to have multiple incisions, each one coming in its own proper place on the edge of the bone, so that you have saws for every test. And this is the form of the three kinds of saws:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	Li qualitez por percier entor l'os brisiet est que tu mettes le tarere sus l'os, et tourne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l'espaice de l'os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu poues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l'os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have cut the bone, and dressed it, if there is anything that remains on the bone that cannot be reached by any other instrument like an incisor, but rather must be more delicate and subtle than the others; and if nothing of the small bones or scales remain, but they are easily removed with instruments; then cure the wound as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another manner of work is this, which the Gauls say is better; and it is loved very much, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover a part of the bone, where or at which there is an opening due to the break, so that when you have uncovered that part, you put below it the head of this cuneiform incision, because it is in this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and it is the part weak in both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then with a small hammer above, so that you lightly copy the bone all around, and be well protected from the cloth that is under; if it is scraped against the bone, so take away gently, because one takes away pain with injury, and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	Instruct the patient to cover with cloth until the break is clean and the bone has been struck only from above and there are small pieces, then it will heal in response to that roughness and remove the scales with a subtle scraper which you should have various quantities for each person so that they can be most convenient according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have many rough scrapers and after that more subtle ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other capillary measures and subtle breaks, it is necessary to adapt your approach according to its direction; and this is something that has no reply from one who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the syphilitic is uncovered, it is necessary that you apply a linen bandage according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another doubled bandage in II or III, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first one; and do this more lightly than you can, so as not to press the syphilitic, and administer from above another binding, and do not pull it tightly except when the wound is healed solely; and leave it for one day or two, until the swellings in the chest are allayed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lizard roots, and wheat flour, and incense powder, and similar things; and make a powder, and apply it to the wound, and administer medicinal poultices according to mastication; and be sure that the wound is healed clean, so that you do not leave any ointment, nor allow any bowels to assemble on the brain, for when bowels assemble on the linen of the brain, they become corrupted and bring great evil to the patient, because when anything sharp is applied to the syphilitic, it poisons from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Prepare yourself then, if no other accidents occur to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful at all.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if nothing happens but for the medicine we have put on him, which has some virtue, then it is fitting to take a piece of honey, three parts of rose oil, and in glue I bind, and place it on the wound; then administer cures in various ways until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both of the two bones above are broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and that one is cartilaginous, and it does not break, unless it bends or twists, and then becomes ill.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, it is fitting that you put your little thumb or index finger into the break and put it back inside the bone, in the pouch, as much as possible, until the bone returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, so that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the arm and cannot come to its natural place, then you must put equal weight on the head of a rod one finger’s breadth.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, do it again and hasten to restore the first day, if you can; but if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the swelling has subsided, then wrap with cloth of linen around the head of the arm as tightly as possible, if the break is in one place.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you put the other part, if it is broken; and the wraps should be so thick that they fill up the empty spaces of the arm.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And it was said by a restorer that one should moisten the wraps in butter and move each person every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but it is likely that they are moist in the making of a certain mixture of fire and powder; then let the tent come loose, until the bones are set hard, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And at no time should you put on or in the nose of an owl in its place, and if it has a swelled joint, and holds the fracture, and blows the patient into calmness; then make look what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the nose while you are working on it, apply a clot or cotton soaked in oil rose or in the poultice of dung.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscess comes, apply a plaster made from flour of sintering, and powder of incense, mixed with fire mixture; then put on light plates, and do not tie the nose; and if the fracture near the nose is small, and it is broken into little pieces, if you have available instruments for this, then cut the slit, and cure the thing that has been injured by soldering, just as plasters and ointments are suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the nose, apply the treatment of the tent, and put in caudles of onions, until it is sane.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the cutting of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is cut under, and there is no wound except for a mere separation without any breaking in two, only cracking within, if one examines closely.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the separation is on the right side, that you put your thumb inside the patient's mouth; and if it is on the left jawbone, put your thumb in the right hand, and gently push the separation into it, and tie off the wound with a thread.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone separation is occurring in two parts, it is necessary that you extend both parts to make them even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth happen, or a fracture, so tie up with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken mandible the cerote, and put on the double drapel; and put on the double drapel an estele well made, or a piece of leather long and wide according to the mandible, and bind it above what you can, and command the patient to rest, and serve light viands.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure has changed, so take him back to the fourth day, and then put back on what is being called a changeling; and apply plaster over it, with powder of the mill with a great amount of wine or fine flour, after having removed the cerote; and put on the linen plaster, light and thin, if the plaster sets, and if the patient's disposition does not change, let him remain until he is cured; many times are cured in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, so that you have said this many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if it has a break and wound together, reward yourself that no piece of the bone remains in place; so subtle is the removal of the bone, which is fitting for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, so enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, then sew the wound, if it is large, and put on fine stitches according to this, for the health of the patient, until he is well.
de la forcele	of the pulse.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The pulse is broken more than once before the shoulder, and the break occurs in three ways: either it is shattered and separated into two parts, with fragments, and this heals lighter to restore; or there is a break with an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Instruct the patient so that when the break is in the sense of the pain, you have two ministers, one who tightens the shoulder so that it feels the breaking force; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put equal the break to your hands, so that the form be as it should be, and there be neither appearance nor swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if it is your work to further extend, then put under the patient an iron sphere round of cloth or linen, so that it be thick according to your need; and press and lift the pain, and restrain the sphere with your hand, so that you put equal the break, as it should.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot treat the head of the pain before, because it comes in deep, then it is fitting that the patient lie on his back and put a moist pillow under the shoulder; and let the ministers put the shoulder down, until the bones of the pain are lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then direct the break to your two feet, and if you find debris, it is suitable to cut through; and carefully take out the pieces lightly, and if the bones cannot join again for any reason, cut at one of the joints that you have; but put this instrument beneath the force, in order to ward off its syphilitic.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it resembles a spoon, and is not made of wood, and so large as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and has two handles, just like you see, and one wide and the other narrow, just like the roughness of the wound that you have made when cutting the bones; and when you are sure about the abscess location, then cut the wound, and if the roughness is small, or you doubt about the abscess location, then apply the wound with drapes and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If an abscess comes to a head, then apply the following remedies: pour olive oil, ash, and wine into the dressing.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The straining of the bone, when it is feeling pains and swelling, is that you put on the bone the plaster made of powder from the mill and honey, and put light stones upon it; and if there is need, place a spear under the collarbone; then take a very large bandage one palm wide, and put a double layer of dressings above the stones, and the plaster; then take a thin needle three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the head of the bandage remains on top; and place the needle above the break, and twist the bandage over the shoulderbone, and under the collarbone, and under the injured side; and loosen each part, and when you see that the joint is in place immediately, and you clearly see that the needle does not move over the broken bone, then reapply every day, and when the joints become stiff, put a small pillow under the collarbone, to lift the shoulder up; this will alleviate the break of the bone by the stretching of the shoulder, or by holding the arm against the chest, until no harm occurs after twenty days; then reapply the plaster, if you see that it is needed, and tighten and leave it thus, until it is restored; and it is restored in twenty-eight days, and less in some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of shoulder break
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	For the shoulder break, it is that if the shoulder breaks or widens, it does not heal unless by its touch; and when you put it back according to the shape of the break, and reset according to its natural form, in all sorts of ways as you can; then put on the shoulder a powder from flour with plenty of wine, and light poultices, and put on two cloths double; then put on a large and subtle needle, one piece more wide than the shoulder, and so gently sew it down at some point near the shoulder, if you sew those stitches of linen so that the needle cuts evenly; and then tie it with a strong band tightly, so that the needle does not move from its place, and watch the knot each day; and every time he loosens, do tighten, and put again the needle when it is out of place, and apply to the patient on his chest; and the shoulder will be restored in twenty days or twenty-five.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a piece of the bone breaks off and does not protrude below the level, push up and make it so that the bone is in place, and do what we have said for soothing an abscessed cavity.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the foot.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The piece is never broken in its middle, but this happens rarely, however it breaks often outside.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it inclines downward and causes the patient great pain, and lack of appetite, and nausea, and by chance vomiting blood, and opening the veins in the broken bone, and they feel very well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient becomes strong again on his two feet, and he puts a strip between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the two breastbones with both hands, and subtly puts equal pressure in all ways so that the figure of the bone is as it should be; then puts on plaster and strips over the subtle point of salt, or another lighter substance, and wraps it up in a bandage, and ties it above the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turns the tie round to the back, and restrains immediately, and rewards each hour with a tightening, and if it loosens, he re-strains; and if it seems necessary to release, because of corruption or itching that comes to him, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and release, and scrape off the plaster, and address whatever is left in ways of cures; then remove the plaster, and restrain until he is well.
de la brisure des costes	of the breast
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Says that the breast injury occurs only in the thick part after the back, and at the head inside, and bends only because they are curved; and one feels pain very much in the examination of this.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatments if are that you set the injury equal, just as it should.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put plaster and bind with a splint, if you need to.
