Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breast injury is turned inward towards the chest, the patient feels great pain, and puncture, just like from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; they are afflicted with pain and vomiting, and have a great bloody discharge, and that's due to bad health, and the old ones have put great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if to those who say it must be administered foods that swell the belly, in order to put an end to the fracture outside.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, unless it has come to us.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes to us, then we are healed.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And none of us said to put poultices on the limb, in order to drain the pus, and it seems like a good reason; everyone agrees, there is doubt that the poultice does not attract the excess fluid to the limb due to its weak state.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And none of us said to cover the limb with a moist cloth in hot oil, and place linen tents between the ribs to straighten the line of the limbs, then either be cured by bleeding, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient when they feel great pain from the bone that presses on their skin, and doubt is at the patient, if it is fitting to split across the broken ribcage, and if you have some instrument to ward off the splinter; and then one must cut into the bone, and treat lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if they are great, and heal with emplastrages, until they are sane.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes on the joint, put moist drapery in oil rose on it, and put on the joint; treat until the joint is healed as it needs to be cut open, and gather fat on the costal side where it must, until they are sane.
de la brisure dou col	of a broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	There is no break when the collarbone is broken, and there is little pain; and so also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens without a break, and you see if it will heal or not, if you take care, so that you see if your hands are softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move or stretch, and when you press them with an needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that certain dispositions are mortal, and if they are mute and feel well when you strangle them and press points, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will recover, if they receive treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing occurs at the spine of the back, and you see if it will heal or not, take care if the feet are soft, and if the accidents are in the hands, and when they suddenly fall with weightlessness and excretion without voluntary movement; and when you have sovineity on their abdomen, they fall with excretion without voluntary movement.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is sitting on his back and it begins to swell, then it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	They say it is deadly: if you do not work on his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen, then the thing is even lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the healer says that if he has an abscess hot, you should apply oil of rose or oil of poppy on the spine until it is soothed; then put on a comfortable plaster and bandage it with a string, and tell the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is cured.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is broken, it is convenient to cover the wound; and take out the bone, then reassemble the two lips of the wound, if they are great, with a suture, until he is cured; and if the joint of the bone is broken, which is called the "joint of the knee", put your left handbag on it and place it equally between both hands on the forearm, then apply the plaster and splint, if necessary; then bind it, and if there is a bone that has been severed, they will have to reattach it, take out the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the bone of the shin
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	There is little chance that the bone of the shin will be fractured, and if it has, even then if it had been only a slight softening at the head; and let them stand long, and incline to the bend, and this will come to the patient pain in the leg, swelling, and point, and inflammation where the fracture.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand upon it, so far as you are above the fracture; and know which way the fracture lies and its shape; and if the fracture is solely at the head, then put equal this fracture, until it has returned to natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it inclines inward, then make the patient lie on his belly, so that the restoration of this fracture becomes apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have set it even, put on the plaster, then put on a stake of wood or bone, and hold the break tight, so that it does not move; and place the limb under the ribs, until they are level.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to lie on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes in, do not touch it, until the abscess is healed, and put on what we have said before; and then return to restoration, and hold it as needed, unless there is some other bad injury; that is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder break
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that part between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of the two methods: one being that you take a stick of wood plaited with middle thread, in this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie both shoulders to the necks, and let them be in place above, and secure the patient on one side; then take off the broken arm at the shoulder, until it comes to the joint, and let him have an artery of bone, then put above any heavy thing or have the ministers stretch it away; then tie up with a bandage the break so that the break returns as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is to suspend the patient above his head, and tie his hand to his neck; then command the two ministers that one ties what is above the break to his hands, and the other ties below to all the joints, and stretch each one to their side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see the extraction is more forceful, then tie below both the joint and the break, and above the break, and stretch each one of the ministers to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the fracture is close to the shoulder blade, you should put a strong line under the humerus and another under the collarbone; and if it's near the collarbone, you should put a lighter one, with care, until the fracture is even on both bones and the collarbone. Then apply the fracture, as it seems right, and secure it, if an abscess does not come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess comes out, do not secure it for seven days, and put a moist cloth in silk and olive oil until the abscess subsides; then secure it. And the way to secure it is that you put plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm back onto the shoulder blade, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the side; put a dressing, and secure onto the shoulder blade and the arm, so that the arm is straight again, unless anything prevents it, or the bone does not move.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bones move, use a rod, and place one end on the break a larger and stronger rod than the others, and put two spaces between each rod, so that each rod is as large as it will pass through the break three times of each part; then strain the rods, in such a way as I have said at the beginning of this chapter, making them stronger and less loose.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see the arrangement of the rods and the straining, as we have said, in the wound where you restore the broken limb, and you doubt whether the abscess is small, if you leave it for seven days, as we have said; then look at each third day the bond, when inflammation does not appear or there is no discharge, or the swelling will not come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the pain, just as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if such an accident does not occur, just let him lie on his back, with his hands over his stomach, and place the bandage under the head, in one hundred and more pinches of linen evenly, and observe each hour of the day or night, until the broken figure of the limb moves or softens the ligaments; then let him take medicine by virtue of the art, and give him the meat which we have before placed before him, in such a manner that the meat be first finely pounded; and when he begins to recover, it is thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary to take back the bandage and the limb after forty days of all, so then let him be dislocated and administered bath and medicine for ease.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If the stricture is swollen and blocked, let it remain tied for three or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made of two bones, which are called the two "fossicles", because one is small, and that one contains the pouch; and the other is large, and that one is below the small bone; by chance, only the larger bone may be broken alone, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is lighter, and the healing; and when the large bone is broken, so is the healing, and it is much more grievous than when both together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bone that is broken alone, then it must be extended lightly, and put equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	In the case of great swelling, they should strain it more strongly; and stretch it upwards towards the cussin, and pull the pouch of his hand higher than that of other people, and his fingers lower than those of other people, so that he crosses them over himself, and stretches the cussin before him higher, so that the patient may suffer no pain or labor; then extend the ministers with both hands to the part below their own hand, or near the joint, and one minister with another above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then put him on an equal surface, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If in the breakage there are pieces, put each one on its own place, and if it has no excess that can bear the weight, and you cannot restore it to its original place, then take out and treat as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If there is an open wound with a break, I have spoken to the single surgeon about it; take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	If in the beginning of the restoration it serves up pus and blood, then put a dressing made of cerote oil of rose and white wax on it, so that neither be too hard nor too soft; and tie the dressing gently from above, until the pus is appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then put the cerote back, and apply an ointment of powdered millet flour mixed with a lot of oil, because you place the stitches, and so that the first stitch be stronger than the others; and know that there should be six stitches or more in this disposition: either the break is in one of the bones or two; and tie it tighter above the break than elsewhere, and every day less when moving it, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter; and so that the dressings on top of the break are soft and moist, and not too hard nor rough; and the threads, from which it is strained, of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and its connection after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident happens to the limb, as if it itches in the same way that itch comes on the limb, then you should raise the limb over hot water, until the itching is relieved; and let the limb not be too tightly pressed.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the binding, and if the ligament is loose and the bone will set, and a similar thing, address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care so that the swellings do not come back to the limb, because it is too tightly bound, then you should loosen it a little, and let it remain thus for some days, until the swellings have gone away, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If no such things come to the patient as we have said, then they will be free from illness for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and then he bends his hands to his neck, and makes them even, and holds back movement and flexion, and lies on his back; and knows that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the composition and temperament of the bodily virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of a hand break
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Knows that at the back of the hand and near the joints there often occur breakages, but only a pleurisy many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And if the finger of the hand is broken or inflamed, it is fitting that the patient should tie a cross around his chest and sit upright always; then he puts his hand on an extended shoulder, and stretches out the jointed bones, and makes them even the fingers, so they are well joined; and he applies plaster and bandages, unless abscesses occur, then he puts in one needle according to the size of him; and it is wrapped up in a cloth of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	If the fracture is in the pelvis near the vent of the joint, make a spere of bandages and instruct the patient to wrap it around his fractured knee; and then tighten it with a length of rope, so that the swelling equals the size of the broken joint, and tighten as much as is needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is in the forearm, so that it may be straightened and put together, place a splint on top and another below the knee joint, so that the wrist is straight and upright, then tie everything around the hand tightly, and secure the bandage between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture occurs on either of the two bones, if it is swollen, place an equal splint, as needed; and tie with the joint, and if you see fit to place a straight small splint to lift the fracture, without movement; and if the fracture is in other places, such as the index or another place, place an equal splint, and secure the bandage with the healthy bone that follows; or tie all of them together, holding fast until it can be moved, or placing a splint on top, as needed; take care with the restoration and arrangement of the abscess site, and cure those who come to you, just as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the broken hip is often fractured, and it can be seen when it turns in front and behind; and the treatment is to tie up the above part and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patients are brought to their face, and then each of these doctors extends the ministers' bandage equally; and it is when the fracture is made in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the hip, so that one of the bandages goes around the joint and the others go below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the genital area, and thus one goes around the groin, and the other extends below; then put on the mirrors so that the bone matches its two hands, in accordance with its natural figure, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, lest there come infection from the abscess.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If it has an abscess on its surface, then let it be treated so that the inflammation goes away and it comes back to its original shape and condition; this is done in that way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is fitting that you wrap the bandage around the fracture with a double or triple cloth, and keep the swelling there, then turn the leg so that the toes point to the root of the nail, and insert one long thread between the thigh and the leg, under the skin, and tie the head of the thread above; then turn up the leg and the thigh with the bandage, then apply splints to the fracture, and place a splint on the bone of the leg; then use a soft cloth to wrap between the leg and the thigh to tighten it evenly, then begin to bind with three or four strips around the fracture; and as you go higher up on the fracture, the tighter the bandage becomes; then tie in two threads that you have inserted between the leg and the thigh, and apply three more splints above, then return below the head of the thread, until you see the foot; and if it stays still, leave it so, and if it does not come back with any swelling or inflammation or other signs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens so that the joint dislocates and addresses itself in that way, as we have said many times before; and if there are pieces of bone that grasp at it, he should cover them with an ointment, just like us. If it cannot be done, then they should split the limb, and scrape on it; and the cure will do what we have said, until he is sane.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no time is lost when the joint breaks just like when we put in a splint, as in the shoulder and arm; because then, whatever treatment is done will not fail the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And knows that the joint is restored in three days, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of the complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin's channel
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	The joints of the lower back have some breaks but they bend many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then it's just a crack or a split, and it wounds and hurts to touch.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when you put equal weight on both sides until it is assembled again, then apply plaster, and if needed, put an iron ring around it, secure it as necessary, then return to all the dispositions we have said for other breaks, just as for abscesses and other appearances; applying each accident as necessary, until he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg break
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It has two bones in the leg, one called "mustelz" and the other called "foscile", just like the arm; and all other breakages are as they come to the arm, and therefore restoration is equal for both, and all wounds are dealt with. And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, then turn them around.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, then feel great pain and see it well; and turn them below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And therefore apply extension, and put it even, and tie the splints equally; but however, if the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the extension should be less and lighter; and tie according to its strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two flaxen straps that pinch the leg from one side and the other, and be long enough from the knee down to the elbow; then tie them again on top and below, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and thus is well done; and no one should put a strap as long as the leg, except for one, and he puts it on the leg to keep movement, and this is done properly in the break where there has been an injury; and move each limb every day to see if there is an abscess or another accident; until the cure when he is sane.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of bones from the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but sometimes a break in the bones of the foot occurs and swelling also, and it does not often come from any other condition.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if he has a break in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones protruding one over another, so put the patient's foot on the ground, just as if he were walking, and then place your foot upon his, so that the bone rises; then press it firmly until they come into their proper position; then apply plaster and dressings to, and make a small table of wood with two chairs flat, at the foot of the patient's foot, then bind him to the foot in that way, and do other things as you find necessary.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three days or four will have passed, if you loosen the ligament, for you will find the bones equal, broken, or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any broken toes, if you restore them, as we have said about the two toes of the hand; then put a splint on the broken toe according to its length, and make it slightly wider, then place above the foot that which I have told, and the splinter will happen immediately. And if there are two or three, or more, broken, if you put one splint on each according to its quantity, wrapped in an I of linen rope, and tie the splint under the foot; and while standing over the head of the splint, away from the belly of the foot, so that it tightens well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you not forget the other things I have said about other breaks, since we have spoken of them; and heal each accident as it is fitting.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break in the finger bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman is broken, if it grows larger, then incline it to the back of the spine, and keep it there behind; then fill the wound with linen cloth as thick as I said; and bind it so tightly that it slowly comes out, bit by bit, until it reaches the entrance of the woman's body, and returns to its normal shape; and when she urinates, if the cloth gets stuck, take it out afterwards, and do this for seven days before: then the break will be restored, and you should see, take a vessel made of wool, and tie a cord around the wound, and pour the entire vessel into the woman's body; then blow into the cord firmly, until the vessel is emptied inside: the nature will return to fix the break; then fill it with linen cloth again, and let it be so for some days, until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the little finger of the hand is broken, or of the woman, so it is restored as we have said in the bone of the hazelnut; and these close breaks are not hidden by those who put their study and use on them, and listen to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break means more deaths on the straight road of restoration; then therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the phallus, when it is broken, take an owl's wing and apply it to the wound; then envelop a cloth around, and leave it for three days or longer, and he will be quickly cured.
de brisure avec plaie	of breaks with wounds.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is for him who has breaks with wounds, especially if it is great, just like the bone of the shoulder or arm or similar, that he will be cured now, provided the cures we have said testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, then you must keep it moist with vinegar, for if you have no other remedy, and you do not come across any poultice, then reapply the wound in the same hour, or on the following day.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If poultices come across on the following day, you must leave the treatment until the next day after a new application, until the poultice is applied again, and do not touch it or apply it on the first day or the second, for you will bring forth bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken and appears near the joint of the finger uncovered, it is to your advantage that you put it on a lighter pin very gently with your fingers.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if you don't have an instrument prepared to put it on equal with your hands, and the limb is held by this iron instrument which has 7 or 8 fingers of length, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; then it is the duty of the apothecary that he grips it 3 or 4 times, according as he needs in each cure of fracture; and it should be thin and a little pointy, so that it doesn't bend under compression on your affected limb, and it should be blunt before, and thick from the middle towards the front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for that's why the curved head of the knife must be placed above the bone of the skull; and strike once, until it comes back, and make them equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the splints cannot well grasp the bone, so it's fitting that you copy the skull of the bone, until the splints have hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone to its proper place, as we have said, then copy it with a suitable instrument, sharp or otherwise, to your best ability; and take out what is stuck in the bone of roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it's not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Si fai tant qu'il soit en son lieu,
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	If the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that it will not happen again, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, so it is not advisable to place a splint; but take instead soft bandages, hard wraps, and tie.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound has not worsened, and you have put on all the vinegar, and applied ointment for healing wounds, just like ointment with four ingredients and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary to lift the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is tender and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the limbs be bandaged in this way, so that the wound opens up lightly downwards.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if each day it trespasses and he cannot heal but has pain in the bowels, see that he has small pieces of bone, because it is necessary to treat the wound with care, and take out all these useless pieces which cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if an abscess comes to the limb, or another kind of corruption, it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter mentioned before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opens on the limb, as it does with the arm or shoulder, and other similar bones of the great members, you do not treat it at first, because many times they die from it, but let it be in that state for a while; by chance, it will shed blood after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	When frost comes upon the snow
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come many times after the health of an injury, especially when it is near the joint, and behold a strange thing about the member, and by chance it cannot restore its natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then take care: if it has come from the cold: administer medicinal remedies such as aloes, incense, and mirrors, and sarcoccolle, acacia, and similar things, just as you pick out any of these things or all together, and mix them with vinegar medicinal or with plenty of wine or with oil; and place on the wound in poultices, and strain well, and do not loosen it in hands for a day; and then loosen it, and continue another, until the nodules are removed; or you strain upon a piece of good pounce; because the properties of pounce are such that they remove all swellings above the members; and if the nodulation is converted into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, as soon as possible, make the superfluousness apparent; or take it to any razor until it is removed, and continue the cure until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A weak member after discharge
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and it remains weak in the limbs and subtle, if it happens for many causes: because one is due to being too tightly tied, and not tightly bound as it was meant to be; or because there are too many ligatures, and the circulation does not come to the limb; or because of excessive swelling; or because of great movements, although not in its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, so weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you feed the patient, and make the body pliable, until blood multiplies in him; and administer baths, and give joy and delight; then apply poultices to the limb, so that the poultice attracts great swelling, and the swelling arises frequently from water, until the swelling reaches the limb; and return it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	One limb twisted after death
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the limb is distorted, do not believe in false remedies which say that you must break the limb anew; for many fools have done this on our earth, and these operations are blamed, and great evils result, and sometimes death follows. Whenever there is nodulation and torture fresh, it is advisable to allow them to arise from hot water or that the herbs be cooked, such as those of valerian, roots, and malloloth, and similar things; and apply a mollifying plaster, just like aqua lion well done, and take the muscillagium of valerian, and mix with fat of geline or oil of sesame, and make it into a paste; or take greasy figs, and grind them with flour of colt's foot, and similar medicines that ease the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes an operation is performed to remove the node due to constant and prolonged friction with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let you move each limb hourly.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the curvature is hardened and aged, like stones, and it requires the removal with iron, then if you wish to cover just beneath the bone, at the subtle incision, lightly; and put a cushion and study in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes on suddenly, if you wish to now return to normal alignment.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, and par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c'on le mueve a l'oure k'il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d'aigue chaude et d'oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, and cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of joint dislocations to be done on a limb.
des mandibules	of jaws or jawbones.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There is often that the jaws are dislocated and swollen, and the dislocations of both jaws occur in two ways: either they are slightly osteoporotic and soft; or they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the chin, and prevent one from closing their mouth, nor can they keep their saliva inside, and swell their tongue with the words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns to its original position with more frequent movements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and done, you must immediately reset it, and do not hesitate; in such a manner that the physicians hold the head of the sick one, and give him a poultice from some of his mouth's blood, on the root of the dislocated jaw within the mouth, because there are two parts if she has dislocations of II pars; and the other two should be held away, to make it even; and instruct the patient to relax his mandibles, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he puts equal poultices on it until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns, weakened, especially if both mandibles are dislocated together, you must apply hot water and oil poultices until it is reset lightly; do not hesitate to restore it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	Et when they are brought back even, and the mouth of the patient is closed by softening, so put moist cloths in rose oil and beeswax on it; then tie it lightly with moist sinews; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his limbs be between two pillows, so that he does not move at all with left or right hand, nor forces himself to stretch, but takes light food until the pains are gone, and the mandibles are numb, and then take what he wants lightly, and does not work hard to open the mouth to suck or to drink, until the mandibles are well numbed and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be returned to their normal position within an hour, and are not converted back to their own place, then it comes to fever, sweating accustomed, and by chance some vomiting of stomach contents.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a sign of death; and many die in seven days.
de la forcelle	of the arm.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The arm cannot be reset along the ribs and the breastbone inside it, and is dislocated again without fail, and you will feel this very much.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And if the treatment is applied so that the patient lies on his back and stretches out his arms; then press his hand into a palm, and it will return; then put on the plaster and bandage, and bind him; and the head of the shoulder which is bent towards the elbow cannot be reset; unless not, and if he dislocates again, then you must reset it to its place, as we have said; then put on the plaster and the bandage, and bind him, and command the patient to rest until he is cured; and thus they are brought back the head of the shoulder when it is bent away from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of a shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Since the shoulder is dislocated in three manners: so that one dislocation occurs at the top of the bone below; and another at the bottom of the bone above; and by chance it dislocates above, which happens rarely; and never behind for the shoulder; nor inside for the nerves; and more often dislocations go below towards the bone, namely to those who have little strength, because they happen suddenly; to those who have enough strength, they happen with pain, and return with pain.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some people that percussion or crushing occurs, and the shoulder swells with an abscess hot, and they think it is dislocated from this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary to examine it, until you are certain; and then begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when they are displaced towards the joint, and you will find the difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find manifest differences between them; and you will find a cavity at the top of the shoulder, and below the joint, the head of the shoulder in the same place as it was before; and neither can the patient return their hand to its normal position, nor move from any movement; and similarly, if she is displaced upwards, she cannot be concealed, because you will find it manifestly at the joint; and this type of dislocation is not very hard to correct, when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	Instruct the patient to lift his hand above, then put your fingers below the wrist, and lift the joint at force upwards into place; and instruct the patient to lift his hand, and stretch it upwards because you have put one below; if it comes to pass suddenly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not happen as we said earlier after some days, it is advisable that the patient be immersed in hot water; and apply an upward-moving mollifying and soothing substance, like a decoction of althaea and fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and have it applied; then place the patient on his back, and put a cloth of linen equal, not too wet nor too dry, under the wrist; and put the mallet's heel on the cloth, and lift the shoulder joint with virtue; and treat the patient's hand; and some other attendants apply the chief of the patient, so that it does not move downward; the shoulder returns completely now, and if you see it is done according to this manner: and you must do that the patient be present for one man who is larger than the patient; and stand upright towards the costal side, and pour water into the spine of the patient from under the wrist, and lift the wrist upward, so that the patient hangs in the air; and some other attendants treat the patient's hand downward towards the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then put with him anything heavy, and now the dislocation returns.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the method is also in another way: and it's like inserting a long iron rod into the ground, so that the joint moves as if pushed by a piston, neither too big nor too small; then put below the patient, but when he has folded himself up well on top, and the patient stands straight with the long stick; then extend his hand towards another part forming, and the joint will return to its place soon; and if it doesn't return for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take an iron rod from two arms of a great one and four of a broad one, which has the head turned back into the hole deep below the plate, according to this shape.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Instruct the patient to lift up his head on a soft cloth, so that it is not struck by the pain of the wound; then put the wound under the saddle of the patient. And extend one arm above the fist of the long one, and bind the handle to the fist, and the arm to the top of the hand, then put the arm above an eschillon (of) a single screw of large size, and so stretch out the hands downwards, and let the body hang from another part: now the joint has returned to its place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is thus in any manner, if you wish to do so, then put the wound under one spear of wool equal, then put the plaster made from powdered flour of the mill, with incense and vinegar on all the shoulder and around it, then draw out from under the saddle soon after, and turn the bandage upon the plaster, and tie the hand to its neck, and so let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he manages little, until the limbs are comforted, because he will recover faster; and then he must manage more after five days or seven, and move him; and if he is firm and not softened, he is cured.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen due to moisture that has come upon it, or for another reason, it is necessary to administer cauterization at three punctures, as he is placed in front of the cauterization instrument.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and the joint dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not stay in place, nor can he lift up one arm towards his shoulder, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either crushed, stretched out, or softened; and know that the joint has never been fixed in its proper place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The displacement that is in the knee and ankles, or behind, if it is done by impulse and extension of hands, and another limb is applied to treat it; and care should be taken until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb becomes inflamed again and moves slowly, then use the patient many times in bath, until that inflammation is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of a shoulder cut
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	That the joint of the shoulder is displaced to one point, and then returns; and if it is displaced in all parts, and even before and behind, and dislocations do not return, because they are seen well and felt well; and displacement according to each type.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick limb with the healthy one, so you can see it open.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is fitting that you reset him so that abscesses come out when they are living, because if the abscess comes out while he's still in his bed, it will be bad for his recovery; and by chance, it may not be possible to fix all of it again, especially when it's in the back; this is worse than other dislocations, and it causes more pain, and by chance, death can come from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is made, when it's such that you can fix it, then you stretch his hand out to your two hands; and his arms should be spread out, and his fingers soft on the joint according to the cut from top to bottom, and behind, and press down the joint into its sockets or to the root of his palm, until it comes back to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there is a dislocation ahead, so it returns when he doubles his hand to its hand, and proud of the root of the palm, which is damaged.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, administer a strong extension; and if two ministers extend the arm, and tie up both hands of each minister, so that he will not move at the extension; then turn the arm in each direction, after having passed over a double length and width of cloth; and when the fingers grasp the joint with their hand, pour oil on them to soften the joint, then set the joint straight, until it returns; and when it is back in place, tie a bandage stiff with vinegar and onion, and strain the arm, and bend the elbow towards the patient's shoulder, and let it rest for some time, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firm in its place, then free the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not tighten well, then re-apply the ointment and the ligament, and leave it for some days, until it is firmly fixed; then release.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels great pain after the return of the joint, and it is still stiff, then bathe him thoroughly and rub him well, and press until he is relieved; or you put on the joint a piece of fat mutton salted meat, then leave it for one day and one night, then take out, and let him enter the bath; and when he sweats, if you rub the joint moderately, then put on the meat again, and then enter the bath; and do this twice or three times, until he is cured; and if you see that you put on a piece of vinegar-soaked fat that has been heated with butter, and stretch it over the joint; he will return to his normal state.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand dislocates and the return is lighter than all other joints. Therefore it must be returned to its place hastily, in the same place where it has dislocated, so that the swelling subsides, or the abscess comes to a head.
