Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, he puts his patient's back against a table, and ties his fingers over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, this is good; but if not, if the strain of applying poultices to a wound calms an abscess, then let him leave it so and try again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If he cannot bear it, and you can't put him back to normal after some days, the joint will remain distorted; and there is no remedy for the patient except that his hands become swollen, and he cannot stretch or strain anything: thus you know that the nerves are injured, or the arteries. For if there's no other cause than applying poultices on the wound, by cautery of the skin, perhaps it's worth trying only to alleviate his condition.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hands are in the right place, put on the poultice as we said, then apply the strain and let him rest for a day, then lift it again.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot be moved well, and there is no injury, so apply the poultice of hot water, and rub it until he is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of both hands.

des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocation of the knee
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is known that the joints of the knee and shoulder only come to dislocations, not like other joints; and the joint of the knee is displaced according to four parts: inside and out, and in front of and behind; and more so when it is displaced inward and less so when it is displaced forward or backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of dislocations inside is that when one joins the ill leg to the healthy one, it extends more, and the patient's knees are wider than the healthy ones, and the patient cannot double their knee joint by fire; and because the swellings of the groin come from there, due to the incision of the abscess.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the signs of him to whom it happens at night, is that this accident are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom it happens in front, is that he stands well with his leg according to the completion; he cannot walk without pain, and double flexing the knee causes pain, and if one wants to make him go, he will not be able, and holds back his urine, and swells the groin, and when he walks, it passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom it happens behind, is that he cannot expand his knee, nor double up, and this leg is crooked more than the other, and the groin area is softened, and the head of the femur is displaced downward below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The signs of this resemblance to dislocation are that if you repair it as the dislocation is old, and it stays according to its position, there is no cure; and it is not advisable to trust him.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this one where the dislocation is fresh, and it's of four kinds of dislocation, hurry up so you restore the joint, and push it inside and outside, and let it move to the right and left; by chance if it returns, and there's no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, you should bind the leg with two strong ropes, or tie the knee; and one other minister will stretch his hand up in such a manner that he pours out his hands underneath his arse, then ties him to a soft rope on the chest; and another stretches the head tightly to the binding; and they all stretch up and down once, until the patient is lifted from the ground once, and remains there.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This is a common method of stretching, which has four similarities, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it's true.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not the case, it's advisable to apply treatment to its similarity When dislocations are present in the armpit area, so that you lift the patient on his sound side, then place a strip on the root of the shoulder, and the one that is below the angle, then tighten the strip upwards towards the angle, and towards the elbow; then grasp other assistants with your arms and hug the large strip of the ill-fated shoulder, stretch it away from the form: if it returns to its position now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot squeeze it in this manner as we have said, it's advisable to tie both feet and the patient together with a strong rope on both ankles and knees; then stretch out the ill-fated leg two times more than the others; then hang him by the head of a stick on high, above the ground two hands' length; then command one minister to hug the shoulder, and let other ministers hang with the patient, who hug together in such a way that the joint returns quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation. S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.

And if dislocation is at the outer side, it is not advisable to stretch the diseased limb after or raise it up from the ground, but rather to keep it as it was before the dislocation, as we have said when lying on both hanches; and let its face be turned upwards, and the ligament stretched as we have said before, and must press firmly on the joint at the table; and will be ready when the diseased limbs are extended and they are even; then add the cups, and put the plaster, and the strain of a bandage, so that the hanch does not move; and it should rest for three days or four, then take off the plaster, and put it back; and if you see that they are even, so as before, and leave the strain for three days; then take off the plaster, and let him walk nicely, until the members are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The gall bladder is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and it should not be displaced forward.

de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocated ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are sometimes swollen and sometimes completely dislocated, and sometimes both swelling and displacement.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And if there are signs that the ankle is swollen and then completely dislocated, and within and behind the part where it is dislocated: the treatment is lighter, and you must stretch it lightly with your hands when it is only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, it is best to have the patient sit upright, and you must press firmly on the knee above the ankle; then take hold of the leg with your right hand, and then again with your left hand twice, then stretch it up high, and pour the foot into it very thoroughly in the highest part; and do this twice, as we have said, putting and taking the foot; if it returns, that is good; but if not, since it will return, then do so; and if it cannot be set thus, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and fix a tight bandage between his thighs, to prevent the patient from bleeding; then press the knee, and other ministers stretch the leg straight out with hands or binding above the knee; then stretch each minister equally, so that the bandage may be fastened between the thighs of the patient to hold him when you stretch him; then place the ligaments equal to the dislocation in his hands, and other ministers stretch the healthy leg below, so that the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it comes to the point, he puts on the plaster and the binding strips, and they form a strait, and he ties the foot to the leg, and wards off the nerves that are above the ankle, so that the joints are not too tight; then he lets him be for two days or three, and if the straiting is loosened, he lets it; then he removes it on the fourth day or a quarter, and they have to go with their malady for four days; and if he goes before this time, it's not sure that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes on the foot, he should soften it, just as we have said elsewhere, until it is cured.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, they should be properly extended with work, and it's a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the case of dislocation at either the neck or foot, if it is not done on a level surface, sit the patient on a level plain or table so that his feet are straight. Put your foot above the opening of these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until he regains feeling; and when it is even, and there is no opening, put under the plant of the foot a wooden board with two joints, then press firmly again, and leave three days, then release him; and make him rest, so that he may be healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wounds come with dislocation, and you try to restore it, many patients die: do not be presumptuous in the cure, unless you are knowledgeable in the art and have used it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and slow to act, but rather harsh; use at the beginning gentle measures to treat the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand, unless you see no hope of recovery; and when you see hope, then restore the limb now as soon as the swelling begins to go away; and when the limb is restored, administer gentle measures to treat the wound, just as it seems fitting, with bandages that have dried out; and if there is a fracture of the dislocation, and small bones are broken, fix the bones, and do what we have said for simple diseases; and beware not to enter into a path of fear, according to what I have said, because this will be meted out to you according to your Creator, and according to the wisdom of your arm and body.
Amen	Amen
